      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carchemish" title="Battle of Carchemish">
       Battle of Carchemish
      </a>
      four years later, and further conflict between the Babylonians and the 26th dynasty of Egypt is recorded during 601586 BCE. According to the bible, this culminated in 586 BCE when Jerusalem and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Temple" title="First Temple">
       First Temple
      </a>
      were destroyed by the Babylonian king
      <a href="/wiki/Nebuchadnezzar_II" title="Nebuchadnezzar II">
       Nebuchadnezzar II
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MFA_40-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-MFA-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most of the surviving Israelite leaders, and much of the other local population, were
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_captivity" title="Babylonian captivity">
       deported to Babylonia
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp6_32-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp6-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Persian_.28Achaemenid.29_Empire_period">
       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">
        Persian (Achaemenid) Empire
       </a>
       period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Persian (Achaemenid) Empire period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_achaemenid_empire_en.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="869" data-file-width="1676" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Map_achaemenid_empire_en.png/220px-Map_achaemenid_empire_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Map_achaemenid_empire_en.png/330px-Map_achaemenid_empire_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Map_achaemenid_empire_en.png/440px-Map_achaemenid_empire_en.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_achaemenid_empire_en.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Achaemenid Empire under Darius III
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Yehud_Medinata" title="Yehud Medinata">
       Yehud Medinata
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Following King
      <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great" title="Cyrus the Great">
       Cyrus the Great
      </a>
      's defeat of the
      <a href="/wiki/Neo-Babylonian_Empire" title="Neo-Babylonian Empire">
       Neo-Babylonian Empire
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Opis" title="Battle of Opis">
       Battle of Opis
      </a>
      , the region became part of the
      <a href="/wiki/Eber-Nari" title="Eber-Nari">
       Eber-Nari
      </a>
      satrapy or
      <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_the_Achaemenid_Empire#Fifth_district" title="Districts of the Achaemenid Empire">
       District number V
      </a>
      (corresponding the regions of (
      <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
       Syria
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
       Phoenicia
      </a>
      , Palestine and
      <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
       Cyprus
      </a>
      ) according to
      <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">
       Herodotus
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Arrian" title="Arrian">
       Arrian
      </a>
      , which included three administrative areas: Phoenicia, Judah and Samaria, and the Arabian tribes. The Phoenician cities of Tyre, Sidon, Byblos, and Aradus were vassal states ruled by hereditary local kings who struck their own silver coins and whose power was limited by the Persian satrap and local popular assemblies. The economies of these cities were mainly based on maritime trade. During military operations, the Phoenicians were obliged to put their fleet at the disposal of the Persian kings. Judah and Samaria enjoyed considerable internal autonomy. Bullae and seal impressions of the end of the 6th and beginning of the 5th centuries mention the province of Judah. Its governors included Sheshbazzar and Zerubbabel under Cyrus and Darius I; Nehemiah; Bagohi, who succeeded Nehemiah and whose ethnicity is difficult to determine; and "Yehizkiyah the governor" and "Yohanan the priest", known from coins struck in Judah in the 4th century BCE. From the second half of the 5th century the province of Samaria was governed by Sanballat and his descendants.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      According to the
      <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">
       bible
      </a>
      and implications from the
      <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_Cylinder" title="Cyrus Cylinder">
       Cyrus Cylinder
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
       Jews
      </a>
      were allowed to return to what their holy books had termed the Land of Israel, and having been granted some autonomy by the Persian administration, it was during this period that the Second Temple in Jerusalem was built.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp6_32-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp6-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edelman_61-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Edelman-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Samaria#Sebastia" title="Samaria">
       Sebastia
      </a>
      , near
      <a href="/wiki/Nablus" title="Nablus">
       Nablus
      </a>
      , was the northernmost province of the Persian administration in Palestine, and its southern borders were drawn at
      <a href="/wiki/Hebron" title="Hebron">
       Hebron
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp6_32-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp6-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-palestineeb_62-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-palestineeb-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some of the local population served as soldiers and lay people in the Persian administration, while others continued to agriculture. In 400 BCE, the
      <a href="/wiki/Nabataeans" title="Nabataeans">
       Nabataeans
      </a>
      made inroads into southern Palestine and built a separate civilization in the
      <a href="/wiki/Negev" title="Negev">
       Negev
      </a>
      that lasted until 160 BCE.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp6_32-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp6-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Avdat_63-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Avdat-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The end of the Persian period was marked by a number of revolts in the region, including a significant uprising against
      <a href="/wiki/Artaxerxes_III" title="Artaxerxes III">
       Artaxerxes III
      </a>
      in 350 BCE, which resulted in the destruction of Jerusalem.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_antiquity">
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">
        Classical antiquity
       </a>
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Classical antiquity">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Hellenic_Kingdoms_.28Ptolemaic_.2F_Seleucid_.2F_Hasmonean.29_period">
       Hellenic Kingdoms (
       <a href="/wiki/Ptolemaic_dynasty" title="Ptolemaic dynasty">
        Ptolemaic
       </a>
       /
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seleucid" title="Seleucid">
        Seleucid
       </a>
       /
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hasmonean" title="Hasmonean">
        Hasmonean
       </a>
       ) period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Hellenic Kingdoms (Ptolemaic / Seleucid / Hasmonean) period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="567" data-file-width="1205" height="104" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg/220px-Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg/330px-Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg/440px-Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Seleucid Empire in c. 200 BCE
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1stMithritadicwar89BC.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="791" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/1stMithritadicwar89BC.png/220px-1stMithritadicwar89BC.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/1stMithritadicwar89BC.png/330px-1stMithritadicwar89BC.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/1stMithritadicwar89BC.png/440px-1stMithritadicwar89BC.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1stMithritadicwar89BC.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Hasmonoen Kingdom at its greatest extent under
        <a href="/wiki/Salome_Alexandra" title="Salome Alexandra">
         Salome Alexandra
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the late 330s BCE,
      <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">
       Alexander the Great
      </a>
      conquered the region, during his six-year
      <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Macedonians" title="Ancient Macedonians">
       Macedonian
      </a>
      conquest of the empire of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darius_III_of_Persia" title="Darius III of Persia">
       Darius III of Persia
      </a>
      . Alexander's armies took Palestine without complication while traveling to Egypt after the
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Tyre_(332_BC)" title="Siege of Tyre (332 BC)">
       Siege of Tyre
      </a>
      , beginning an important period of Hellenistic influence in the land.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp7_64-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp7-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hooker_65-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hooker-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During 323301 BCE, the region changed hands numerous times during the
      <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Diadochi" title="Wars of the Diadochi">
       wars of the Diadochi
      </a>
      , with rulers including
      <a href="/wiki/Laomedon_of_Mytilene" title="Laomedon of Mytilene">
       Laomedon of Mytilene
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_I_Soter" title="Ptolemy I Soter">
       Ptolemy I Soter
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Antigonus_I_Monophthalmus" title="Antigonus I Monophthalmus">
       Antigonus I Monophthalmus
      </a>
      . In 312 BCE
      <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_I_Soter" title="Ptolemy I Soter">
       Ptolemy I Soter
      </a>
      defeated Antigonus' son
      <a href="/wiki/Demetrius_I_of_Macedon" title="Demetrius I of Macedon">
       Demetrius I
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gaza_(312_BC)" title="Battle of Gaza (312 BC)">
       Battle of Gaza
      </a>
      , but withdrew from the region shortly thereafter. It is probable that
      <a href="/wiki/Seleucus_I_Nicator" title="Seleucus I Nicator">
       Seleucus I Nicator
      </a>
      , then an Admiral under Ptolemy's command, took part in the battle, as following the battle he was given 800 infantry and 200 cavalry and immediately travelled to
      <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">
       Babylon
      </a>
      where he founded the
      <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">
       Seleucid Empire
      </a>
      . The region was finally re-captured by
      <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_I_Soter" title="Ptolemy I Soter">
       Ptolemy I Soter
      </a>
      after
      <a href="/wiki/Antigonus_I_Monophthalmus" title="Antigonus I Monophthalmus">
       Antigonus I Monophthalmus
      </a>
      was killed at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ipsus" title="Battle of Ipsus">
       Battle of Ipsus
      </a>
      . Ptolemy had not taken part in the battle, and the victors
      <a href="/wiki/Seleucus_I_Nicator" title="Seleucus I Nicator">
       Seleucus I Nicator
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Lysimachus" title="Lysimachus">
       Lysimachus
      </a>
      had carved up the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antigonid" title="Antigonid">
       Antigonid
      </a>
      Empire between them, with Southern Syria intended to become part of the
      <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">
       Seleucid Empire
      </a>
      . Although
      <a href="/wiki/Seleucus_I_Nicator" title="Seleucus I Nicator">
       Seleucus
      </a>
      did not attempt to conquer the area he was due, Ptolemy's pre-emptive move led to the
      <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Wars" title="Syrian Wars">
       Syrian Wars
      </a>
      , which began in 274 BCE between the successors of the two leaders. The northern portion of Palestine ultimately fell into the hands of the
      <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">
       Seleucid Empire
      </a>
      in 219 through the betrayal of Governor
      <a href="/wiki/Theodotus_of_Aetolia" title="Theodotus of Aetolia">
       Theodotus of Aetolia
      </a>
      , who had held the province on behalf of
      <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_IV_Philopator" title="Ptolemy IV Philopator">
       Ptolemy IV Philopator
      </a>
      . The Seleucids advanced on Egypt, but were defeated at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Raphia" title="Battle of Raphia">
       Battle of Raphia
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">
       Rafah
      </a>
      ) in 217. However, in 200 BCE Southern Palestine also fell under the control of the
      <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">
       Seleucid Empire
      </a>
      following the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Panium" title="Battle of Panium">
       Battle of Panium
      </a>
      (part of the Fifth
      <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Wars" title="Syrian Wars">
       Syrian War
      </a>
      ) in which
      <a href="/wiki/Antiochus_III_the_Great" title="Antiochus III the Great">
       Antiochus III the Great
      </a>
      defeated the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ptolemies" title="Ptolemies">
       Ptolemies
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freep225_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Freep225-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The landscape during this period was markedly changed by extensive growth and development that included urban planning and the establishment of well-built fortified cities.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-palestineeb_62-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-palestineeb-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp7_64-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp7-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic" title="Hellenistic">
       Hellenistic
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">
       pottery
      </a>
      was produced that absorbed Philistine traditions. Trade and commerce flourished, particularly in the most Hellenized areas, such as Ashkelon, Jaffa,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Jerusalem,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gaza,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and ancient Nablus (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tell_Balatah" title="Tell Balatah">
       Tell Balatah
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp7_64-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp7-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Persians had not interfered with the internal affairs of the various subject-peoples of the region, but the Greeks followed a policy of deliberate
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenisation" title="Hellenisation">
       Hellenisation
      </a>
      , encouraging, although not normally enforcing, Greek culture. Hellenisation took root first in the densely settled coastal and lowland areas, and only really began to impinge on more backward areas such as Judea in the early 2nd century. According to
      <a href="/wiki/Josephus" title="Josephus">
       Josephus
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Books_of_the_Maccabees" title="Books of the Maccabees">
       Books of the Maccabees
      </a>
      , the continued Hellenization of Palestine by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seleucid" title="Seleucid">
       Seleucids
      </a>
      resulted in an uprising in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judean_Mountains" title="Judean Mountains">
       Judean Mountains
      </a>
      , known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Maccabees" title="Maccabees">
       Maccabean Revolt
      </a>
      . Although the revolt was quelled in 160 BCE at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Elasa" title="Battle of Elasa">
       Battle of Elasa
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">
       Seleucid Empire
      </a>
      entered a period of rapid decline in 145144 BCE, beginning with the overthrowing of King
      <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Balas" title="Alexander Balas">
       Alexander Balas
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Antioch_(145_BC)" title="Battle of Antioch (145 BC)">
       Battle of Antioch (145 BCE)
      </a>
      (the capital of the empire) by
      <a href="/wiki/Demetrius_II_Nicator" title="Demetrius II Nicator">
       Demetrius II Nicator
      </a>
      in alliance with
      <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_VI_Philometor" title="Ptolemy VI Philometor">
       Ptolemy VI Philometor
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      , as well as the capturing of
      <a href="/wiki/Seleucia" title="Seleucia">
       Seleucia
      </a>
      (the previous capital of the empire) by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mithradates_I_of_Parthia" title="Mithradates I of Parthia">
       Mithradates I of Parthia
      </a>
      . By 116 BCE, a civil war between Seleucid half-brothers
      <a href="/wiki/Antiochus_VIII_Grypus" title="Antiochus VIII Grypus">
       Antiochus VIII Grypus
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Antiochus_IX_Cyzicenus" title="Antiochus IX Cyzicenus">
       Antiochus IX Cyzicenus
      </a>
      resulted in a breakup of the kingdom and the independence of certain principalities, including Judea.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This allowed Judean leader
      <a href="/wiki/John_Hyrcanus" title="John Hyrcanus">
       John Hyrcanus
      </a>
      to carry out the first military conquests of the independent Hasmonean kingdom in 110 BCE, raising a mercenary army to capture
      <a href="/wiki/Madaba" title="Madaba">
       Madaba
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schechem" title="Schechem">
       Schechem
      </a>
      , significantly increasing the regional influence of Jerusalem
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hasmoneans" title="Hasmoneans">
       Hasmoneans
      </a>
      gradually extended their authority over much of the region, forcibly converting the populations of neighbouring regions, and creating a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judean" title="Judean">
       Judean
      </a>
      -
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samaritan" title="Samaritan">
       Samaritan
      </a>
      -
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Idumaean" title="Idumaean">
       Idumaean
      </a>
      -
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ituraean" title="Ituraean">
       Ituraean
      </a>
      -
      <a href="/wiki/Galilean" title="Galilean">
       Galilean
      </a>
      alliance in the process.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mortonsmith210_4-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-mortonsmith210-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Judean (Jewish, see
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ioudaioi" title="Ioudaioi">
       Ioudaioi
      </a>
      ) control over the wider region resulted in it also becoming known as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judaea" title="Judaea">
       Judaea
      </a>
      , a term that had previously only referred to the smaller region of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judean_Mountains" title="Judean Mountains">
       Judean Mountains
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During 7363 BCE, the
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
       Roman Republic
      </a>
      extended its influence into the region in the
      <a href="/wiki/Third_Mithridatic_War" title="Third Mithridatic War">
       Third Mithridatic War
      </a>
      . During the war,
      <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">
       Armenian
      </a>
      King
      <a href="/wiki/Tigranes_the_Great" title="Tigranes the Great">
       Tigranes the Great
      </a>
      took control of Syria and prepared to invade
      <a href="/wiki/Judea" title="Judea">
       Judea
      </a>
      but retreated following an invasion of Armenia by
      <a href="/wiki/Lucullus" title="Lucullus">
       Lucullus
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to Armenian historian
      <a href="/wiki/Movses_Khorenatsi" title="Movses Khorenatsi">
       Movses Khorenatsi
      </a>
      writing in c. 482 CE, Tigranes captured Jerusalem and deported Hyrcanus to Armenia, however most scholars deem this account to be incorrect.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Iudaea_period">
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">
        Roman
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iudaea" title="Iudaea">
        Iudaea
       </a>
       period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Roman Iudaea period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Augusto_30aC_-_6dC_55%25CS_jpg.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1181" data-file-width="1704" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Augusto_30aC_-_6dC_55%25CS_jpg.JPG/220px-Augusto_30aC_-_6dC_55%25CS_jpg.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Augusto_30aC_-_6dC_55%25CS_jpg.JPG/330px-Augusto_30aC_-_6dC_55%25CS_jpg.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Augusto_30aC_-_6dC_55%25CS_jpg.JPG/440px-Augusto_30aC_-_6dC_55%25CS_jpg.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Augusto_30aC_-_6dC_55%25CS_jpg.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Extent of the Roman Empire under Augustus, 30 BCE  6 CE
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Following the
      <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">
       Roman
      </a>
      conquest of Judea led by
      <a href="/wiki/Pompey" title="Pompey">
       Pompey
      </a>
      in 63 BCE,
      <a href="/wiki/Aulus_Gabinius" title="Aulus Gabinius">
       Aulus Gabinius
      </a>
      , proconsul of
      <a href="/wiki/Syria_(Roman_province)#Syria_in_antiquity" title="Syria (Roman province)">
       Syria
      </a>
      , split the former Hasmonean Kingdom into five districts of legal and religious councils known as
      <a href="/wiki/Sanhedrin" title="Sanhedrin">
       sanhedrin
      </a>
      based at Jerusalem,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tzippori" title="Tzippori">
       Sepphoris
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">
       Galilee
      </a>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/Jericho" title="Jericho">
       Jericho
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Amathus,_Palestine" title="Amathus, Palestine">
       Amathus
      </a>
      (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perea_(Bible)" title="Perea (Bible)">
       Perea
      </a>
      ) and
      <a href="/wiki/Umm_Qais" title="Umm Qais">
       Gadara
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Roman rule was solidified when
      <a href="/wiki/Herod_the_Great" title="Herod the Great">
       Herod
      </a>
      , whose dynasty was of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Idumean" title="Idumean">
       Idumean
      </a>
      ancestry, was appointed as king.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp7_64-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp7-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_83-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Britannica-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Following a brief intervention by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacorus_I_of_Parthia" title="Pacorus I of Parthia">
       Pacorus I of Parthia
      </a>
      , from 37
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iudaea" title="Iudaea">
       Iudaea
      </a>
      under
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herod_I" title="Herod I">
       Herod I
      </a>
      was a client kingdom of the
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
       Roman Empire
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Urban planning under the Romans was characterized by cities designed around the Forumthe central intersection of two main streetsthe
      <a href="/wiki/Cardo" title="Cardo">
       Cardo
      </a>
      , running north-south and the
      <a href="/wiki/Decumanus_Maximus" title="Decumanus Maximus">
       Decumanus
      </a>
      running east-west.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNESCO_84-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cities were connected by an extensive road network developed for economic and military purposes. Among the most notable archaeological remnants from this era are
      <a href="/wiki/Herodium" title="Herodium">
       Herodium
      </a>
      (Tel al-Fureidis) to the south of Bethlehem,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herodium_85-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Herodium-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Masada" title="Masada">
       Masada
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Caesarea_Maritima" title="Caesarea Maritima">
       Caesarea Maritima
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp7_64-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp7-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caesarea_86-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Caesarea-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herod%27s_Temple" title="Herod's Temple">
       Herod arranged a renovation
      </a>
      of the Second Temple in Jerusalem, with a massive expansion of the Temple Mount platform and major expansion of the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Temple" title="Second Temple">
       Jewish Temple
      </a>
      around 19 BCE. The Temple Mount's natural plateau was extended by enclosing the area with four massive retaining walls and filling the voids. This artificial expansion resulted in a large flat expanse, which today forms the eastern section of the Old City of Jerusalem.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Around the time associated with the birth of
      <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">
       Jesus
      </a>
      , Roman Palestine was in a state of disarray and direct Roman rule was re-established.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp7_64-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp7-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNRV_87-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UNRV-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 6 CE, the Herodian governorate ended with the deposition of
      <a href="/wiki/Herod_Archelaus" title="Herod Archelaus">
       Herod Archelaus
      </a>
      as the
      <a href="/wiki/Ethnarch" title="Ethnarch">
       ethnarch
      </a>
      of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tetrarchy_(Judea)" title="Tetrarchy (Judea)">
       Tetrarchy of Judea
      </a>
      . The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herodian_Dynasty" title="Herodian Dynasty">
       Herodian Dynasty
      </a>
      was then replaced by Roman
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prefects" title="Prefects">
       prefects
      </a>
      and after 44 CE by
      <a href="/wiki/Procurator_(Roman)" title="Procurator (Roman)">
       procurators
      </a>
      , beginning with
      <a href="/wiki/Coponius" title="Coponius">
       Coponius
      </a>
      .
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herodian_Dynasty" title="Herodian Dynasty">
       Herodians
      </a>
      continued to rule elsewhere in Palestine. Senator
      <a href="/wiki/Quirinius" title="Quirinius">
       Quirinius
      </a>
      was appointed
      <a href="/wiki/Legatus" title="Legatus">
       Legate
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Syria_(Roman_province)" title="Syria (Roman province)">
       Roman province of Syria
      </a>
      (to which Judea had been "added" according to
      <a href="/wiki/Josephus" title="Josephus">
       Josephus
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      though
      <a href="/wiki/Hayim_Hillel_Ben-Sasson" title="Hayim Hillel Ben-Sasson">
       Ben-Sasson
      </a>
      claims it was a "satellite of Syria" and not "legally part of Syria"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ) and carried out the tax census of both Syria and Judea known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Census_of_Quirinius" title="Census of Quirinius">
       Census of Quirinius
      </a>
      .
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caesarea_Palaestina" title="Caesarea Palaestina">
       Caesarea Palaestina
      </a>
      replaced Jerusalem as the administrative capital of the region.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Most scholars agree that Jesus was a
      <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">
       Galilean
      </a>
      Jew, born around the beginning of the first century,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEK.C3.B6stenbergerKellumQuarles2009114_91-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEK.C3.B6stenbergerKellumQuarles2009114-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaier1989124_92-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaier1989124-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and hold that Jesus lived in Galilee and Judea and did not preach or study elsewhere.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreenMcKnightMarshall1992442_93-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreenMcKnightMarshall1992442-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dunn303_94-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dunn303-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrossanWatts199928.E2.80.9329_95-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrossanWatts199928.E2.80.9329-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Using the gospel accounts with historical data, most scholars arrive at a date of birth between 6 and 4 CE for Jesus,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vermes2006_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Vermes2006-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDunn2003324_97-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDunn2003324-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but some propose estimates that lie in a wider range.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFor_example.2C_John_P._Meier_states_that_Jesus.27_birth_year_is_.27.27c..27.27_7.2F6_BC.2C.7FUNIQ--ref-00000173-QINU.7F_while_Finegan_favors_.27.27c..27.27_3.2F2_BC..7FUNIQ--ref-00000176-QINU.7F_100-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFor_example.2C_John_P._Meier_states_that_Jesus.27_birth_year_is_.27.27c..27.27_7.2F6_BC.2C.7FUNIQ--ref-00000173-QINU.7F_while_Finegan_favors_.27.27c..27.27_3.2F2_BC..7FUNIQ--ref-00000176-QINU.7F-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The general scholarly consensus is that Jesus was a contemporary of
      <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">
       John the Baptist
      </a>
      and was crucified by Roman governor
      <a href="/wiki/Pontius_Pilate" title="Pontius Pilate">
       Pontius Pilate
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevine20064_101-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevine20064-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most scholars agree that
      <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">
       his crucifixion
      </a>
      was between 30 and 33 CE.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Humphreys1992_102-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Humphreys1992-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEK.C3.B6stenbergerKellumQuarles2009398_103-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEK.C3.B6stenbergerKellumQuarles2009398-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As a result of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Jewish-Roman_War" title="First Jewish-Roman War">
       First Jewish-Roman War
      </a>
      (6673),
      <a href="/wiki/Titus" title="Titus">
       Titus
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(70)" title="Siege of Jerusalem (70)">
       sacked Jerusalem
      </a>
      (in 70 CE) destroying the Second Temple, leaving only supporting walls, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Wall" title="Western Wall">
       Western Wall
      </a>
      . According to
      <a href="/wiki/Josephus" title="Josephus">
       Josephus
      </a>
      , the estimated death toll was 250,0001,100,000.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharisee" title="Pharisee">
       Pharisee
      </a>
      rabbi
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yokhanan_ben_Zakai" title="Yokhanan ben Zakai">
       Yokhanan ben Zakai
      </a>
      , a student of
      <a href="/wiki/Hillel_the_Elder" title="Hillel the Elder">
       Hillel
      </a>
      , fled during the siege of Jerusalem to negotiate with the Roman General
      <a href="/wiki/Titus" title="Titus">
       Titus
      </a>
      . Yokhanan obtained permission to reestablish a
      <a href="/wiki/Sanhedrin" title="Sanhedrin">
       Sanhedrin
      </a>
      in the coastal city of
      <i>
       Iamnia
      </i>
      (modern
      <a href="/wiki/Yavne" title="Yavne">
       Yavne
      </a>
      ) (see also
      <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Jamnia" title="Council of Jamnia">
       Council of Jamnia
      </a>
      ). He founded a school of
      <a href="/wiki/Torah" title="Torah">
       Torah
      </a>
      there that would eventually evolve, through the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mishna" title="Mishna">
       Mishna
      </a>
      in around 200 CE, into
      <a href="/wiki/Rabbinic_Judaism" title="Rabbinic Judaism">
       Rabbinic Judaism
      </a>
      . The region's leading
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">
       Christians
      </a>
      (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Christians" title="Jewish Christians">
       Jewish Christians
      </a>
      ) relocated to
      <a href="/wiki/Pella,_Jordan" title="Pella, Jordan">
       Pella
      </a>
      . Other Jewish groups such as
      <a href="/wiki/Sadducees" title="Sadducees">
       Sadducees
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Essenes" title="Essenes">
       Essenes
      </a>
      are no longer recorded as groups in history.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 106 CE, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nabatean" title="Nabatean">
       Nabatean
      </a>
      territory was incorporated into the Roman province of Arabia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Syria_Palaestina_period">
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Syria_Palaestina" title="Syria Palaestina">
        Syria Palaestina
       </a>
       period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Roman Syria Palaestina period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_125.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1817" data-file-width="2186" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Roman_Empire_125.png/220px-Roman_Empire_125.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Roman_Empire_125.png/330px-Roman_Empire_125.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Roman_Empire_125.png/440px-Roman_Empire_125.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_125.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Roman empire at its peak under Hadrian showing the location of the Roman legions deployed in 125 CE
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 132 CE, the Emperor
      <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">
       Hadrian
      </a>
      joined the province of Iudaea (comprising Samaria, Judea proper, and Idumea) with
      <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">
       Galilee
      </a>
      to form new province of
      <a href="/wiki/Syria_Palaestina" title="Syria Palaestina">
       Syria Palaestina
      </a>
      . Hadrian probably chose a name that revived the ancient name of Philistia (Palestine), combining it with that of the neighboring province of Syria, in an attempt to suppress Jewish connection to the land.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-H.H._Ben-Sasson.2C_1976.2C_page_334_105-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-H.H._Ben-Sasson.2C_1976.2C_page_334-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However Cassius Dio, the Roman historian from whom we have the bulk of our understanding of the revolt, does not mention the change of name nor the reason behind it in his "Roman History".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Jerusalem was renamed "
      <a href="/wiki/Aelia_Capitolina" title="Aelia Capitolina">
       Aelia Capitolina
      </a>
      " and temples were built there to honor Roman gods, particularly
      <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_(mythology)" title="Jupiter (mythology)">
       Jupiter
      </a>
      . In 135 CE, the victory in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bar_Kokhba%27s_revolt" title="Bar Kokhba's revolt">
       Bar Kokhba's revolt
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">
       Hadrian
      </a>
      resulted in 580,000 Jews killed (according to
      <a href="/wiki/Cassius_Dio" title="Cassius Dio">
       Cassius Dio
      </a>
      ) and destabilization of the region's Jewish population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lehmann_109-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lehmann-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      was re-established as the Roman military colony of
      <a href="/wiki/Aelia_Capitolina" title="Aelia Capitolina">
       Aelia Capitolina
      </a>
      ; a largely unsuccessful attempt was made to prevent Jews and Christians from living there. Many Jews and Christians left Palestine altogether for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Diaspora" title="Jewish Diaspora">
       Diaspora
      </a>
      communities, and large numbers of prisoners of war were sold as
      <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">
       slaves
      </a>
      throughout the Empire. Christianity in particular was practiced in secret and the
      <a href="/wiki/Hellenization" title="Hellenization">
       Hellenization
      </a>
      of Palestine continued under
      <a href="/wiki/Septimius_Severus" title="Septimius Severus">
       Septimius Severus
      </a>
      (193211 CE).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp7_64-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp7-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      New pagan cities were founded in Judea at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleutheropolis" title="Eleutheropolis">
       Eleutheropolis
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Bayt_Jibrin" title="Bayt Jibrin">
       Bayt Jibrin
      </a>
      ), Diopolis (
      <a href="/wiki/Lod" title="Lod">
       Lydd
      </a>
      ), and
      <a href="/wiki/Emmaus_Nicopolis" title="Emmaus Nicopolis">
       Nicopolis
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Emmaus_Nicopolis" title="Emmaus Nicopolis">
       Emmaus
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-palestineeb_62-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-palestineeb-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp7_64-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp7-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some two hundred Jewish communities remained, as gradually certain religious freedoms were restored, such as exemption from the imperial cult and internal self-administration. The Romans made no such concession to the Samaritans, to whom religious liberties were denied, while their sanctuary on Mt.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gerizim" title="Gerizim">
       Gerizim
      </a>
      was defiled by a pagan temple, as part of measures were taken to suppress the resurgence of Samaritan nationalism.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lehmann_109-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lehmann-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A number of events with far-reaching consequences took place during this period, including further religious
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schism_(religion)" title="Schism (religion)">
       schisms
      </a>
      between
      <a href="/wiki/Split_of_early_Christianity_and_Judaism" title="Split of early Christianity and Judaism">
       Christianity and Rabbinic Judaism
      </a>
      such as a council held by the bishops of Palestine in Caesarea in 195 that decreed that
      <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">
       Easter
      </a>
      was to be always kept on a Sunday, and not with the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Passover" title="Jewish Passover">
       Jewish Passover
      </a>
      . The Romans destroyed the community of the Mother Church in Jerusalem, which had existed since the time of Jesus
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The line of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Patriarch_of_Jerusalem#Bishops_of_Jerusalem" title="Orthodox Patriarch of Jerusalem">
       Jewish bishops in Jerusalem
      </a>
      , which is claimed to have started with Jesus's brother
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_the_Just" title="James the Just">
       James the Righteous
      </a>
      as its first bishop, ceased to exist, within the Empire. Hans Kung suggests that the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Christians" title="Jewish Christians">
       Jewish Christians
      </a>
      sought refuge in Arabia and he quotes with approval a view that this created a paradox of truly world-historical significance that while Jewish Christianity was swallowed up in the Christian church, it preserved itself in Islam.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During 259272, the region fell under the rule of
      <a href="/wiki/Odaenathus" title="Odaenathus">
       Odaenathus
      </a>
      as King of the
      <a href="/wiki/Palmyrene_Empire" title="Palmyrene Empire">
       Palmyrene Empire
      </a>
      after the capture of Emperor
      <a href="/wiki/Valerian_(emperor)" title="Valerian (emperor)">
       Valerian
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Shapur_I" title="Shapur I">
       Shapur I
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Edessa" title="Battle of Edessa">
       Battle of Edessa
      </a>
      caused the
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
       Roman Empire
      </a>
      to splinter until
      <a href="/wiki/Aurelian" title="Aurelian">
       Aurelian
      </a>
      defeated the
      <a href="/wiki/Palmyrene_Empire" title="Palmyrene Empire">
       Palmyrenes
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Emesa" title="Battle of Emesa">
       Battle of Emesa
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Homs" title="Homs">
       Homs
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Late_Antiquity_period">
       <a href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" title="Late Antiquity">
        Late Antiquity
       </a>
       period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Late Antiquity period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Late_Roman_Empire_period">
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Roman_Empire" title="Late Roman Empire">
        Late Roman Empire
       </a>
       period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Late Roman Empire period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:476eur.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="411" data-file-width="620" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/476eur.jpg/220px-476eur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/476eur.jpg/330px-476eur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/476eur.jpg/440px-476eur.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:476eur.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Byzantine Empire in 476
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Following the victory of Christian emperor
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constantine_I" title="Constantine I">
       Constantine
      </a>
      in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_Wars_of_the_Tetrarchy_(306%E2%80%93324)" title="Civil Wars of the Tetrarchy (306324)">
       Civil Wars of the Tetrarchy (306324)
      </a>
      , the total Christianization of the Roman Empire began.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp8_112-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp8-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cohen_113-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Cohen-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Within a few months, the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Council_of_Nicaea" title="First Council of Nicaea">
       First Council of Nicaea
      </a>
      (first worldwide Christian council) confirmed the status of
      <a href="/wiki/Aelia_Capitolina" title="Aelia Capitolina">
       Aelia (Jerusalem)
      </a>
      as a patriarchate,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      at which point the city is generally taken to have been renamed Jerusalem.
      <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">
       Theodosius I
      </a>
      declared
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/State_church_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="State church of the Roman Empire">
       state religion of the empire
      </a>
      in 380, and Palestine became part of the
      <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
       Eastern Roman Empire
      </a>
      ("Byzantium") after the division of the Roman Empire into east and west (a fitful process that was not finalized until 395 CE).
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Israel_Byzantine_5c.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="839" data-file-width="707" height="356" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Israel_Byzantine_5c.jpg/300px-Israel_Byzantine_5c.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Israel_Byzantine_5c.jpg/450px-Israel_Byzantine_5c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Israel_Byzantine_5c.jpg/600px-Israel_Byzantine_5c.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Israel_Byzantine_5c.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        5th-century CE: Byzantine provinces of
        <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Prima" title="Palaestina Prima">
         Palaestina I
        </a>
        (Philistia, Judea and Samaria) and
        <i>
         Palaestina II
        </i>
        (Galilee and Perea)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Byzantines redrew the borders of the Land of Palestine. The various Roman provinces (Syria Palaestina, Samaria, Galilee, and Peraea) were reorganized into three diocese of Palaestina, reverting to the name first used by Greek historian
      <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">
       Herodotus
      </a>
      in the mid-5th century BCE:
      <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Prima" title="Palaestina Prima">
       Palaestina Prima
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Secunda" title="Palaestina Secunda">
       Secunda
      </a>
      , and Tertia or Salutaris (First, Second, and Third Palestine), part of the
      <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_the_East" title="Diocese of the East">
       Diocese of the East
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp8_112-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp8-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimesIdniopulos_115-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYTimesIdniopulos-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Palaestina Prima
      </i>
      consisted of Judea,
      <a href="/wiki/Samaria" title="Samaria">
       Samaria
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Paralia_(Palestine)" title="Paralia (Palestine)">
       Paralia
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perea_(Holy_Land)" title="Perea (Holy Land)">
       Peraea
      </a>
      with the governor residing in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caesarea_Palaestina" title="Caesarea Palaestina">
       Caesarea
      </a>
      .
      <i>
       Palaestina Secunda
      </i>
      consisted of the Galilee, the lower
      <a href="/wiki/Jezreel_Valley" title="Jezreel Valley">
       Jezreel Valley
      </a>
      , the regions east of Galilee, and the western part of the former
      <a href="/wiki/Decapolis" title="Decapolis">
       Decapolis
      </a>
      with the seat of government at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scythopolis" title="Scythopolis">
       Scythopolis
      </a>
      .
      <i>
       Palaestina Tertia
      </i>
      included the Negev, southern Jordanonce part of Arabiaand most of
      <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">
       Sinai
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Petra" title="Petra">
       Petra
      </a>
      as the usual residence of the governor. Palestina Tertia was also known as Palaestina Salutaris.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp8_112-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp8-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salutaris_116-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Salutaris-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to historian H.H. Ben-Sasson,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      this reorganisation took place under
      <a href="/wiki/Diocletian" title="Diocletian">
       Diocletian
      </a>
      (284305), although other scholars suggest this change occurred later in 390.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      This was the period of Palestine's greatest prosperity in antiquity.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Urbanization increased, large new areas were put under cultivation, monasteries proliferated and synagogues were restored. The cities of Palestine, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Caesarea_Maritima" title="Caesarea Maritima">
       Caesarea Maritima
      </a>
      , Jerusalem, Scythopolis,
      <a href="/wiki/Nablus" title="Nablus">
       Neapolis
      </a>
      , and Gaza reached their peak population, and the population West of the Jordan may have reached as many as one million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lehmann_109-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lehmann-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Bede" title="Bede">
       Bede
      </a>
      in his
      <i>
       Historia Ecclesiastica
      </i>
      , drew on
      <a href="/wiki/Orosius" title="Orosius">
       Orosius
      </a>
      ' information gathered from the local Jews to describe Palestine as one of the provinces of "Syria, which is called
      <a href="/wiki/Haran" title="Haran">
       Aran
      </a>
      by the
      <a href="/wiki/Hebrews" title="Hebrews">
       Hebrews
      </a>
      . The place is between the River Euphrates and the
      <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
       Great Sea
      </a>
      , and extends towards Egypt; its largest provinces are
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commagene" title="Commagene">
       Commagene
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
       Phoenicia
      </a>
      , and Palestine, as well as the countries of the
      <a href="/wiki/Saracen" title="Saracen">
       Saraceni
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Nabataeans" title="Nabataeans">
       Nabathaei
      </a>
      . It has twelve
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Gens" title="Gens">
        gentes
       </a>
      </i>
      ."54
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 326,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constantine_I" title="Constantine I">
       Constantine
      </a>
      's mother
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Helena_(Empress)" title="Helena (Empress)">
       Saint Helena
      </a>
      visited
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      and ordered the destruction of
      <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">
       Hadrian
      </a>
      's temple to
      <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">
       Venus
      </a>
      , which had been built on
      <a href="/wiki/Calvary" title="Calvary">
       Calvary
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp8_112-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp8-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Accompanied by
      <a href="/wiki/Macarius_of_Jerusalem" title="Macarius of Jerusalem">
       Macarius of Jerusalem
      </a>
      , the excavation reportedly discovered the
      <a href="/wiki/True_Cross" title="True Cross">
       True Cross
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Tunic" title="Holy Tunic">
       Holy Tunic
      </a>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Nails" title="Holy Nails">
       Holy Nails
      </a>
      . The first
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulcher" title="Church of the Holy Sepulcher">
       Church of the Holy Sepulcher
      </a>
      in Jerusalem, the first
      <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Nativity" title="Church of the Nativity">
       Church of the Nativity
      </a>
      in Bethlehem and the first
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Church_of_the_Ascension,_Jerusalem&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Church of the Ascension, Jerusalem (page does not exist)">
       Church of the Ascension
      </a>
      on the Mount of Olives were all built during Constantine's reign.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp8_112-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp8-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Christian_monasticism_before_451" title="Christian monasticism before 451">
       earliest monasteries in Christianity
      </a>
      outside of Egypt were built in Palestine during this period,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-palestineeb_62-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-palestineeb-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp8_112-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp8-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      notably those of
      <a href="/wiki/Hilarion" title="Hilarion">
       Hilarion
      </a>
      near Gaza,
      <a href="/wiki/Epiphanius_of_Salamis" title="Epiphanius of Salamis">
       Saint Epiphanius
      </a>
      at Ad near the city of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleutheropolis" title="Eleutheropolis">
       Eleutheropolis
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Bayt_Jibrin" title="Bayt Jibrin">
       Bayt Jibrin
      </a>
      , the head of the largest bishopric in Palestine at this time),
      <a href="/wiki/Tyrannius_Rufinus" title="Tyrannius Rufinus">
       Tyrannius Rufinus
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Melania_the_Elder" title="Melania the Elder">
       Melania the Elder
      </a>
      on the
      <a href="/wiki/Mount_of_Olives" title="Mount of Olives">
       Mount of Olives
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Euthymius_the_Great" title="Euthymius the Great">
       Euthymius the Great
      </a>
      at Pharan,
      <a href="/wiki/Sabbas_the_Sanctified" title="Sabbas the Sanctified">
       Sabbas the Sanctified
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Kidron_Valley" title="Kidron Valley">
       Kidron Valley
      </a>
      as well as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Monastery_(Wadi_Qelt)" title="St. George's Monastery (Wadi Qelt)">
       St. George's Monastery
      </a>
      in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wadi_al-Qelt" title="Wadi al-Qelt">
       Wadi al-Qelt
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Monastery_of_the_Temptation" title="Monastery of the Temptation">
       Monastery of the Temptation
      </a>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Deir_Hajla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Deir Hajla (page does not exist)">
       Deir Hajla
      </a>
      near
      <a href="/wiki/Jericho" title="Jericho">
       Jericho
      </a>
      , and Deir
      <a href="/wiki/Mar_Saba" title="Mar Saba">
       Mar Saba
      </a>
      and Deir
      <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">
       Theodosius
      </a>
      east of Bethlehem.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp8_112-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp8-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The sack of Rome in 410 caused a significant episode of migration to Palestine as a group of aristocratic ladies responded to the holy man Jerome's invitation to settle in Aelia Capitolina and Bethlehem.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lehmann_109-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lehmann-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 451, the
      <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Chalcedon" title="Council of Chalcedon">
       Council of Chalcedon
      </a>
      confirmed Jerusalem's status as a
      <a href="/wiki/Patriarchate" title="Patriarchate">
       Patriarchate
      </a>
      as one of the
      <a href="/wiki/Pentarchy" title="Pentarchy">
       Pentarchy
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Juvenal_of_Jerusalem" title="Juvenal of Jerusalem">
       Juvenal of Jerusalem
      </a>
      became the first
      <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Patriarch_of_Jerusalem" title="Greek Orthodox Patriarch of Jerusalem">
       Patriarch of Jerusalem
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horn2008_p.60_119-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Horn2008_p.60-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Notable works by Christian scholars were produced in Palestine in the disciplines of
      <a href="/wiki/Rhetoric" title="Rhetoric">
       rhetoric
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Historiography" title="Historiography">
       historiography
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eusebius_of_Caesarea" title="Eusebius of Caesarea">
       Eusebian ecclesiastical history
      </a>
      , classicizing history and
      <a href="/wiki/Hagiography" title="Hagiography">
       hagiography
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holum_120-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Holum-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Saint
      <a href="/wiki/Cyril_of_Jerusalem" title="Cyril of Jerusalem">
       Cyril of Jerusalem
      </a>
      delivered his
      <a href="/wiki/Cyril_of_Jerusalem#Catechetical_Lectures" title="Cyril of Jerusalem">
       Mystagogical Catecheses
      </a>
      , instructions on the principal topics of Christian faith and practise, and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Jerome" title="Saint Jerome">
       Saint Jerome
      </a>
      moved to Jerusalem in order to commence work on the
      <a href="/wiki/Vulgate" title="Vulgate">
       Vulgate
      </a>
      , commissioned by
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_Damasus_I" title="Pope Damasus I">
       Pope Damasus I
      </a>
      and instrumental in the fixation of the
      <a href="/wiki/Biblical_canon" title="Biblical canon">
       Biblical canon
      </a>
      in the West.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Procopius" title="Procopius">
       Procopius
      </a>
      , from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caesarea_Palaestina" title="Caesarea Palaestina">
       Caesarea Palaestina
      </a>
      , became the Byzantine Empire's principal historian of the 6th century, writing the
      <i>
       Wars of Justinian
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       Buildings of Justinian
      </i>
      and the celebrated
      <i>
       Secret History
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palestine_according_to_Eusbius_and_Jerome_-_Smith_1915.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="925" data-file-width="559" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Palestine_according_to_Eusbius_and_Jerome_-_Smith_1915.jpg/150px-Palestine_according_to_Eusbius_and_Jerome_-_Smith_1915.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Palestine_according_to_Eusbius_and_Jerome_-_Smith_1915.jpg/225px-Palestine_according_to_Eusbius_and_Jerome_-_Smith_1915.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Palestine_according_to_Eusbius_and_Jerome_-_Smith_1915.jpg/300px-Palestine_according_to_Eusbius_and_Jerome_-_Smith_1915.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palestine_according_to_Eusbius_and_Jerome_-_Smith_1915.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Palestine according to
        <a href="/wiki/Eusebius" title="Eusebius">
         Eusebius
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Jerome" title="Jerome">
         Jerome
        </a>
        , by
        <a href="/wiki/George_Adam_Smith" title="George Adam Smith">
         George Adam Smith
        </a>
        , 1915
       </div>
