      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Under Byzantine rule, the two dioceses of Palaestina proper became a center of
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      , while retaining significant
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">
       Jewish
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samaritan" title="Samaritan">
       Samaritan
      </a>
      communities. Some areas, like Gaza, were well known as pagan holdouts, and remained attached to the worship of
      <a href="/wiki/Dagon" title="Dagon">
       Dagon
      </a>
      and other deities as their ancestors had been for thousands of years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghassanid" title="Ghassanid">
       Ghassanid
      </a>
      Arab migration in the 4th and 5th centuries established an Arab Christian domain with a capital on the Golan, forming a buffer of Christian Byzantium against the wild tribes of Arabia. The "Life of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Barsauma_of_Samosata&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Barsauma of Samosata (page does not exist)">
       Barsauma of Samosata
      </a>
      ", a 6th-century Christian polemic about the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monophysite" title="Monophysite">
       Monophysite
      </a>
      monk of the early 5th century, stated that Jews, Samaritans and pagans formed a large part of the population and persecuted Christians during this period.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 351352, a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_revolt_against_Gallus" title="Jewish revolt against Gallus">
       Jewish revolt against Byzantine rule
      </a>
      in Tiberias and other parts of the
      <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">
       Galilee
      </a>
      was brutally suppressed. In 361,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoplatonist" title="Neoplatonist">
       Neoplatonist
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate" title="Julian the Apostate">
       Julian the Apostate
      </a>
      becomes
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
       Roman
      </a>
      Emperor and attempted to reverse the growing influence of
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      by encouraging other religions. As a result,
      <a href="/wiki/Alypius_of_Antioch" title="Alypius of Antioch">
       Alypius of Antioch
      </a>
      was commissioned to rebuild the Temple in Jerusalem and Jews were formally allowed to return to the city
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Browning1978_p.176_124-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Browning1978_p.176-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, two years later the
      <a href="/wiki/Galilee_earthquake_of_363" title="Galilee earthquake of 363">
       Galilee earthquake of 363
      </a>
      together with the re-establishment of
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      's dominance following the death of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate" title="Julian the Apostate">
       Julian the Apostate
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Samarra" title="Battle of Samarra">
       Battle of Samarra
      </a>
      ended the attempts to rebuild the Temple. In 438 CE,
      <a href="/wiki/Aelia_Eudocia" title="Aelia Eudocia">
       the Empress Eudocia
      </a>
      allowed Jews to return to Jerusalem to live.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Samaritan self-rule had shortly gained a level of independence under the leadership of
      <a href="/wiki/Baba_Rabba" title="Baba Rabba">
       Baba Rabba
      </a>
      in late 4th century. However, they were again subdued by Byzantine forces. Samaritan attempts to gain independence from Byzantines peaked during the 5th and 6th centuries in a series of
      <a href="/wiki/Samaritan_Revolts" title="Samaritan Revolts">
       Samaritan Revolts
      </a>
      , some of which had messianic aspirations. The outcome of Samaritan strife with Christian Byzantines, supported by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghassanid" title="Ghassanid">
       Ghassanid
      </a>
      Arabs, turned disastrous. After the Third Samaritan revolt in 529531, led by
      <a href="/wiki/Julianus_ben_Sabar" title="Julianus ben Sabar">
       Julianus ben Sabar
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Samaritan_Revolts" title="Samaritan Revolts">
       Fourth Revolt in 555
      </a>
      . With Samaritan casualties went well beyond 100,000, cities and worship places destroyed, many enslaved and expelled, the Samaritan community dwindled.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 1 July 536 CE,
      <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
       Justinian I
      </a>
      promoted Stephanus (Stephen) the governor at
      <a href="/wiki/Caesarea" title="Caesarea">
       Caesarea
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Proconsul" title="Proconsul">
       proconsul
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       anthypatos
      </i>
      ), giving him authority over the two remaining
      <a href="/wiki/Consularis" title="Consularis">
       consulars
      </a>
      . Justinian believed that the elevation of the governor was appropriate because he was responsible for "the province in which our Lord
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" title="Jesus Christ">
       Jesus Christ
      </a>
      ... appeared on earth".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holum_120-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Holum-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PLRE_125-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PLRE-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">
       Justinian I
      </a>
      undertook a number of building works in Jerusalem, including the once magnificent
      <a href="/wiki/Nea_Ekklesia_of_the_Theotokos" title="Nea Ekklesia of the Theotokos">
       Nea Ekklesia of the Theotokos
      </a>
      ("the Nea") and the extension of the
      <a href="/wiki/Cardo" title="Cardo">
       Cardo
      </a>
      thoroughfare.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Present-Day_Palestine_and_the_Holy_Land_-_1400s.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1310" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Present-Day_Palestine_and_the_Holy_Land_-_1400s.png/220px-Present-Day_Palestine_and_the_Holy_Land_-_1400s.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Present-Day_Palestine_and_the_Holy_Land_-_1400s.png/330px-Present-Day_Palestine_and_the_Holy_Land_-_1400s.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Present-Day_Palestine_and_the_Holy_Land_-_1400s.png/440px-Present-Day_Palestine_and_the_Holy_Land_-_1400s.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Present-Day_Palestine_and_the_Holy_Land_-_1400s.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        This map of Palestine and the Holy Land was published in Florence around 1480 and was included in Francesco Berlinghieris expanded edition of Ptolemys Geographia (Geography).
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Byzantine administration of Palestine was temporarily suspended during the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine-Sassanid_War_of_602%E2%80%93628" title="Byzantine-Sassanid War of 602628">
       Persian occupation of 61428
      </a>
      . In 613 CE, the Persian
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanian_Empire" title="Sassanian Empire">
       Sassanian Empire
      </a>
      under
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khosrau_II" title="Khosrau II">
       Khosrau II
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Sassanid_War_of_602%E2%80%93628" title="ByzantineSassanid War of 602628">
       had invaded the Levant
      </a>
      led by General
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shahrbaraz_of_Persia" title="Shahrbaraz of Persia">
       Shahrbaraz
      </a>
      , taking Antioch and later Caesaria. Jews under
      <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_of_Tiberias" title="Benjamin of Tiberias">
       Benjamin of Tiberias
      </a>
      assisted the conquering Persians,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolt_against_Heraclius" title="Revolt against Heraclius">
       revolting
      </a>
      against the Byzantine Empire under
      <a href="/wiki/Heraclius" title="Heraclius">
       Heraclius
      </a>
      and hoping of controlling Jerusalem autonomously. In 614 CE, Persian-Jewish forces
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(614)" title="Siege of Jerusalem (614)">
       conquered Jerusalem
      </a>
      , destroying most of the churches, taking Patriarch
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zacharias_of_Jerusalem&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zacharias of Jerusalem (page does not exist)">
       Zacharias
      </a>
      prisoner, taking the
      <a href="/wiki/True_Cross" title="True Cross">
       True Cross
      </a>
      and other relics to
      <a href="/wiki/Ctesiphon" title="Ctesiphon">
       Ctesiphon
      </a>
      , and massacring much of the Christian population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hussey1961_p.25_127-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hussey1961_p.25-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Jews of Jerusalem gained autonomy to some degree, but frustrated with its limitations and anticipating its loss offered to assist the Byzantines in return for amnesty for the revolt. In 617 CE, the Jewish governor
      <a href="/wiki/Nehemiah_ben_Hushiel" title="Nehemiah ben Hushiel">
       Nehemiah ben Hushiel
      </a>
      was killed by a mob of Christian citizens, three years after his appointment. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanids" title="Sassanids">
       Sassanids
      </a>
      quelled the uprising and appointed a
      <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
       Christian
      </a>
      governor to replace him. At that time the Persians betrayed the agreements with the Jews and expelled the Jewish population from Jerusalem, forbidding them to live within 3 miles (4.8km) of it.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      In 625 CE (or 628 CE), the Byzantinian army returned to the area, promising amnesty to Jews who had joined the Persians, and was greeted by
      <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_of_Tiberias" title="Benjamin of Tiberias">
       Benjamin of Tiberias
      </a>
      . In 629 CE, the Byzantine Emperor Heraclius marched into Jerusalem at the head of his army, following the decisive defeat of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Empire" title="Sassanid Empire">
       Sassanid Empire
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nineveh_(627)" title="Battle of Nineveh (627)">
       Battle of Nineveh (627)
      </a>
      . Heraclius personally returned the
      <a href="/wiki/True_Cross" title="True Cross">
       True Cross
      </a>
      to the city.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nabateans" title="Nabateans">
       Nabateans
      </a>
      roamed the Negev by the Roman Period, and by the Byzantine Period dominated the swath of sparsely populated deserts, from the Sinai to the Negev to the northwest coast of Arabia, the outlands that the Byzantines called the diocese of Palaestina Salutoris (meaning something like "near Palestine"). Its capital Petra was formally the capital of the Roman province of
      <a href="/wiki/Arabia_Petraea" title="Arabia Petraea">
       Arabia Petraea
      </a>
      . The Nabateans also inhabited the outland of Jordan and southern Syria, improperly called the diocese of Arabia because its capital Bostra was within the northern extremity of the Roman province of Arabia Petrae. The origin of the Nabateans remains obscure, but they were
      <a href="/wiki/Aramaic_language" title="Aramaic language">
       Aramaic
      </a>
      speakers, and the term "Nabatean" was the Arabic name for an Aramean of Syria and Iraq. By the 3rd century during the Late Roman Period, the Nabateans stopped writing in Aramaic and began writing in
      <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">
       Greek
      </a>
      , and by the Byzantine Period they converted to Christianity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Trading relations existed between the cities of Palestine and the Arab tribes of the
      <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">
       Hejaz
      </a>
      , particularly with the southern cities of
      <a href="/wiki/Petra" title="Petra">
       Petra
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">
       Gaza
      </a>
      .
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammed" title="Muhammed">
       Muhammed
      </a>
      , his father (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abd_Allah_ibn_Abd_Al_Muttalib" title="Abd Allah ibn Abd Al Muttalib">
       Abd Allah
      </a>
      ) and his great-grandfather (
      <a href="/wiki/Hashim_ibn_%27Abd_Manaf" title="Hashim ibn 'Abd Manaf">
       Hashim
      </a>
      , who died in
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">
       Gaza
      </a>
      ) all travelled on trading routes through the region in the 6th century,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in 583 Muhammed is said to have met with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nestorian_Church" title="Nestorian Church">
       Nestorian
      </a>
      monk
      <a href="/wiki/Bahira" title="Bahira">
       Bahira
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Bosra" title="Bosra">
       Bosra
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From the beginning of
      <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
       Islam
      </a>
      in 610,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Jerusalem became the
      <a href="/wiki/Qibla" title="Qibla">
       Qibla
      </a>
      (focal point for
      <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
       Muslim
      </a>
      prayers) for fourteen years until it was replaced by
      <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">
       Mecca
      </a>
      in 624, 18 months after the
      <a href="/wiki/Hijra_(Islam)" title="Hijra (Islam)">
       Hijra
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">
       Muhammad
      </a>
      's migration to
      <a href="/wiki/Medina" title="Medina">
       Medina
      </a>
      ). According to
      <a href="/wiki/Sahih_al-Bukhari" title="Sahih al-Bukhari">
       Sahih al-Bukhari
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">
       Muhammad
      </a>
      then ordained the
      <a href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Mosque" title="Al-Aqsa Mosque">
       Al-Aqsa Mosque
      </a>
      as one of the three holy mosques of Islam
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
       <a href="#cite_note-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A decade later, Byzantium lost control of the region during the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Syria" title="Muslim conquest of Syria">
       Muslim conquest of Syria
      </a>
      , during which the empire's forces were decisively defeated at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Yarmouk" title="Battle of Yarmouk">
       Battle of Yarmouk
      </a>
      in 636. Jerusalem
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(637)" title="Siege of Jerusalem (637)">
       capitulated
      </a>
      in 638 and Caesarea between 640 and 642.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holum_120-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Holum-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The subsequent
      <a href="/wiki/Rashidun" title="Rashidun">
       Rashidun
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">
       Umayyad Caliphates
      </a>
      saw a century of rapid expansion of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">
       Arab
      </a>
      power well beyond the Arabian peninsula in the form of a vast
      <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
       Muslim
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">
       Arab Empire
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Rashidun.2C_Umayyad_and_Abbasid_Caliphates_period">
       <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">
        Rashidun
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">
        Umayyad
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">
        Abbasid Caliphates
       </a>
       period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Rashidun, Umayyad and Abbasid Caliphates period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_expansion_of_Caliphate.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="900" height="101" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Map_of_expansion_of_Caliphate.svg/220px-Map_of_expansion_of_Caliphate.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Map_of_expansion_of_Caliphate.svg/330px-Map_of_expansion_of_Caliphate.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Map_of_expansion_of_Caliphate.svg/440px-Map_of_expansion_of_Caliphate.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_expansion_of_Caliphate.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The expansion of the caliphate under the Umayyads.
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #a1584e; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         Expansion under Muhammad, 622632
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ef9070; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         Expansion during the Rashidun Caliphate, 632661
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #fad07d; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         Expansion during the Umayyad Caliphate, 661750
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shattering_isochamend.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1304" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Shattering_isochamend.png/220px-Shattering_isochamend.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Shattering_isochamend.png/330px-Shattering_isochamend.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Shattering_isochamend.png/440px-Shattering_isochamend.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shattering_isochamend.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        An anachronistic map of the various de facto independent emirates after the Abbasids lost their military dominance (c. 950).
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 638, following the
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(637)" title="Siege of Jerusalem (637)">
       Siege of Jerusalem
      </a>
      , the Caliph
      <a href="/wiki/Umar" title="Umar">
       Omar Ibn al-Khattab
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Sophronius_of_Jerusalem" title="Sophronius of Jerusalem">
       Safforonius
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Patriarch_of_Jerusalem" title="Greek Orthodox Patriarch of Jerusalem">
       Patriarch
      </a>
      of Jerusalem, signed
      <i>
       Al-Uhda al-'Omariyya
      </i>
      (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Umariyya_Covenant" title="The Umariyya Covenant">
       The Umariyya Covenant
      </a>
      ), an agreement that stipulated the rights and obligations of all non-Muslims in Palestine.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp8_112-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp8-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Christians and Jews were considered
      <a href="/wiki/People_of_the_Book" title="People of the Book">
       People of the Book
      </a>
      , enjoyed some
      <a href="/wiki/Dhimmi" title="Dhimmi">
       protection (dhimmi)
      </a>
      but had to pay a special
      <a href="/wiki/Tax_per_head" title="Tax per head">
       poll tax
      </a>
      called
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jizyah" title="Jizyah">
       jizyah
      </a>
      ("
      <a href="/wiki/Tribute" title="Tribute">
       tribute
      </a>
      ") in return for this protection. According to
      <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_ibn_Jarir_al-Tabari" title="Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari">
       Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari
      </a>
      , the covenant guaranteed Christians freedom of religion but prohibited Jews from living in Jerusalem. However, during the early years of Muslim control of the city, a small permanent Jewish population returned to Jerusalem after a 500-year absence.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Umar" title="Umar">
       Umar
      </a>
      , the second of the initial four
      <a href="/wiki/Rashidun" title="Rashidun">
       Rashidun
      </a>
      Caliphs, was the first conqueror of Jerusalem to enter the city on foot, and when visiting the site that now houses the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haram_al-Sharif" title="Haram al-Sharif">
       Haram al-Sharif
      </a>
      , he declared it a sacred place of prayer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
       <a href="#cite_note-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cities that accepted the new rulers, as recorded in registrars from the time, were: Jerusalem, Nablus,
      <a href="/wiki/Jenin" title="Jenin">
       Jenin
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">
       Acre
      </a>
      , Tiberias,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bet_Shean" title="Bet Shean">
       Bisan
      </a>
      , Caesarea,
      <a href="/wiki/Lajjun" title="Lajjun">
       Lajjun
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Lod" title="Lod">
       Lydd
      </a>
      , Jaffa,
      <a href="/wiki/Imwas" title="Imwas">
       Imwas
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beit_Jibrin" title="Beit Jibrin">
       Beit Jibrin
      </a>
      , Gaza,
      <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">
       Rafah
      </a>
      , Hebron,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yubna" title="Yubna">
       Yubna
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">
       Haifa
      </a>
      , Safed and Ashkelon.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp10_137-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp10-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In Arabic, the area approximating the Byzantine Diocese of Palaestina I in the south (roughly Judea, Philistia, and southern Jordan) was called
      <a href="/wiki/Jund_Filastin" title="Jund Filastin">
       Jund Filastin
      </a>
      (meaning "the military district of Palestine", as a tax administrative area),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the Diocese of Palaestina II in the north (roughly Samaria, Galilee, Golan, and northern Jordan)
      <a href="/wiki/Jund_al-Urdunn" title="Jund al-Urdunn">
       Jund al-Urdunn
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 661, with the assassination of
      <a href="/wiki/Ali" title="Ali">
       Ali
      </a>
      , the last of the Rashidun Caliphs,
      <a href="/wiki/Muawiyah_I" title="Muawiyah I">
       Muawiyah I
      </a>
      became the uncontested Caliph of the Islamic World.
      <a href="/wiki/Muawiyah_I" title="Muawiyah I">
       Muawiyah I
      </a>
      was ordained as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caliph" title="Caliph">
       Caliph
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      , ending the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Fitna" title="First Fitna">
       First Fitna
      </a>
      and marking the beginning of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umayyad" title="Umayyad">
       Umayyad
      </a>
      Empire.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Under
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umayyad" title="Umayyad">
       Umayyad
      </a>
      rule, the Byzantine province of Palaestina Prima became the administrative and military sub-province (
      <i>
       jund
      </i>
      ) of
      <a href="/wiki/Jund_Filastin" title="Jund Filastin">
       Filastin
      </a>
      the Arabic name for Palestine from that point forward.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WKhalidi27_139-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WKhalidi27-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It formed one of five subdivisions of the larger province of
      <i>
       ash-Sham
      </i>
      (Arabic for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilad_ash-Sham" title="Bilad ash-Sham">
       Greater Syria
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gerber_140-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gerber-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Jund_Filastin" title="Jund Filastin">
        Jund Filastin
       </a>
      </i>
      (Arabic  , literally "the army of Palestine") was a region extending from the Sinai to the plain of Acre. Major towns included
      <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">
       Rafah
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Caesarea" title="Caesarea">
       Caesarea
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">
       Gaza
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jaffa" title="Jaffa">
       Jaffa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Nablus" title="Nablus">
       Nablus
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Jericho" title="Jericho">
       Jericho
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parkes_141-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Parkes-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Lod" title="Lod">
       Lod
      </a>
      served as the headquarters of the province of Filastin and the capital later moved to
      <a href="/wiki/Ramla" title="Ramla">
       Ramla
      </a>
      .
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Jund_al-Urdunn" title="Jund al-Urdunn">
        Jund al-Urdunn
       </a>
      </i>
      (literally "the army of Jordan") was a region to the north and east of Filastin, which included the cities of
      <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">
       Acre
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Beit_She%27an" title="Beit She'an">
       Bisan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tiberias" title="Tiberias">
       Tiberias
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parkes_141-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Parkes-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dome_of_the_Rock1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Dome_of_the_Rock1.jpg/220px-Dome_of_the_Rock1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Dome_of_the_Rock1.jpg/330px-Dome_of_the_Rock1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Dome_of_the_Rock1.jpg/440px-Dome_of_the_Rock1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dome_of_the_Rock1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Dome_of_the_Rock" title="Dome of the Rock">
         Dome of the Rock
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 687691, during the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Fitna" title="Second Fitna">
       Second Fitna
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Dome_of_the_Rock" title="Dome of the Rock">
       Dome of the Rock
      </a>
      was built under Caliph
      <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Malik_ibn_Marwan" title="Abd al-Malik ibn Marwan">
       Abd al-Malik ibn Marwan
      </a>
      , becoming the world's first great work of Islamic architecture.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slavik2001_p.60_26-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Slavik2001_p.60-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_Mount" title="Temple Mount">
       Temple Mount
      </a>
      (known as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haram_Ash-Sharif" title="Haram Ash-Sharif">
       Haram Ash-Sharif
      </a>
      in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic" title="Islamic">
       Islamic
      </a>
      world and the site where the Islamic prophet
      <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">
       Muhammad
      </a>
      is believed by Muslims to have begun his nocturnal journey to heaven), had remained unbuilt for c. 600 years since
      <a href="/wiki/Titus" title="Titus">
       Titus
      </a>
      's destruction of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herod%27s_Temple" title="Herod's Temple">
       Herod's Temple
      </a>
      in 70.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      About a decade afterward, Caliph
      <a href="/wiki/Al-Walid_I" title="Al-Walid I">
       Al-Walid I
      </a>
      had the
      <a href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Mosque" title="Al-Aqsa Mosque">
       Al-Aqsa Mosque
      </a>
      built.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Faizer_142-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Faizer-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      It was under Umayyad rule that Christians and Jews were granted the official title of "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peoples_of_the_Book" title="Peoples of the Book">
       Peoples of the Book
      </a>
      " to underline the common monotheistic roots they shared with Islam.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp10_137-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp10-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
       <a href="#cite_note-143">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        143
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Christian pilgrims visited and made generous donations to Christian holy places in Jerusalem and Bethlehem,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp11_144-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp11-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the establishment of the Pilgrims' Inn in Jerusalem during this period was seen as a fulfillment of Umar's pledge to Bishop Sophronious to allow freedom of religion and access to Jerusalem for Christian pilgrims.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MEI_145-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MEI-145">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        145
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Christian monasteries throughout the region continued to operate, and between 730-749
      <a href="/wiki/John_of_Damascus" title="John of Damascus">
       John of Damascus
      </a>
      , previously chief adviser to Caliph
      <a href="/wiki/Hisham_ibn_Abd_al-Malik" title="Hisham ibn Abd al-Malik">
       Hisham ibn Abd al-Malik
      </a>
      , moved to the
      <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">
       monastery
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Mar_Saba" title="Mar Saba">
       Mar Saba
      </a>
      outside Jerusalem and became the major opponent of the
      <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Iconoclasm" title="Byzantine Iconoclasm">
       First Iconoclasm
      </a>
      through his theological writings.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Trading relations between Palestine and Europe were strong, and a trade fair took place in Jerusalem every year on September 15 where merchants from
      <a href="/wiki/Pisa" title="Pisa">
       Pisa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">
       Genoa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">
       Venice
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marseilles" title="Marseilles">
       Marseilles
      </a>
      converged to acquire spices, soaps, silks, olive oil, sugar and glassware in exchange for European products.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp11_144-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp11-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 744 riots broke out in the major cities of
      <a href="/wiki/Palestine" title="Palestine">
       Palestine
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
       Syria
      </a>
      during the reign of
      <a href="/wiki/Marwan_II" title="Marwan II">
       Marwan II
      </a>
      , and were quelled in 7456. These rebellions were followed by further revolts in the East of the empire, which culminated in the defeat of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umayyad" title="Umayyad">
       Umayyad
      </a>
      army in 750 at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Zab" title="Battle of the Zab">
       Battle of the Zab
      </a>
      . The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasids" title="Abbasids">
       Abbasids
      </a>
      took control of the entire empire including Palestine, forcing
      <a href="/wiki/Marwan_II" title="Marwan II">
       Marwan II
      </a>
      to flee via
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">
       Gaza
      </a>
      to Egypt where he was assassinated.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">
       Baghdad
      </a>
      -based
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasid" title="Abbasid">
       Abbasid
      </a>
      Caliphs renovated and visited the holy shrines and sanctuaries in Jerusalem, with
      <a href="/wiki/Al-Mansur" title="Al-Mansur">
       Al-Mansur
      </a>
      arranging in 758 the renovation of the
      <a href="/wiki/Dome_of_the_Rock" title="Dome of the Rock">
       Dome of the Rock
      </a>
      that had collapsed in an earthquake
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
       <a href="#cite_note-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Al-Ma%27mun" title="Al-Ma'mun">
       Al-Ma'mun
      </a>
      arranging further renovations following a visit to
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      in 813.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talhami_147-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Talhami-147">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        147
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Abbasids continued to build up
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramle" title="Ramle">
       Ramle
      </a>
      , which had become the capital of
      <a href="/wiki/Jund_Filastin" title="Jund Filastin">
       Jund Filastin
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp10_137-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp10-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lev_148-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lev-148">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        148
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Coastal areas were fortified and developed and port cities like Acre,
      <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">
       Haifa
      </a>
      , Caesarea,
      <a href="/wiki/Arsuf" title="Arsuf">
       Arsuf
      </a>
      , Jaffa and
      <a href="/wiki/Ashkelon" title="Ashkelon">
       Ashkelon
      </a>
      received monies from the state treasury.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp11_144-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp11-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the Abbasid caliphs visited the region less frequently than the Umayyads since their capital in
      <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">
       Baghdad
      </a>
      was a further 500 miles (800km) east.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasid" title="Abbasid">
       Abbasid
      </a>
      period marked the beginning of the
      <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">
       Islamic Golden Age
      </a>
      , in which a number of scholars from Palestine, such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">
       Gazan
      </a>
      -born jurist and founder of the
      <a href="/wiki/Shafi%27i" title="Shafi'i">
       Shafi'i
      </a>
      school of
      <a href="/wiki/Fiqh" title="Fiqh">
       fiqh
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_ibn_Idris_ash-Shafi%60i" title="Muhammad ibn Idris ash-Shafi`i">
       Muhammad ibn Idris ash-Shafi`i
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalemite
      </a>
      geographer
      <a href="/wiki/Al-Muqaddasi" title="Al-Muqaddasi">
       Al-Muqaddasi
      </a>
      , played an integral part.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The influence of the Arabian tribes declined during the Abbasid period and the only context where they are reported is in uprising against the central authority.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gil283_149-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gil283-149">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        149
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, a dispute between the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mudhar" title="Mudhar">
       Mudhar
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yamani" title="Yamani">
       Yamani
      </a>
      tribes broke out in
      <a href="/wiki/Jund_al-Urdunn" title="Jund al-Urdunn">
       Jund al-Urdunn
      </a>
      towards the end of the 8th century leading to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_War_in_Palestine_(793%E2%80%93796)" title="Civil War in Palestine (793796)">
       Civil War in Palestine (793796)
      </a>
      . Harun al-Rashid viewed this as a rebellion and sent a large army under
      <a href="/wiki/Ja%27far_ibn_Yahya" title="Ja'far ibn Yahya">
       Ja'far ibn Yahya al-Barmaki
      </a>
      to quell the revolt. According to historian Moshe Gil, "he put down the rebels with an iron hand and much blood was spilled."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gil283_149-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gil283-149">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        149
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The cities of
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">
       Gaza
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bayt_Jibrin" title="Bayt Jibrin">
       Bayt Jibrin
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ashkelon" title="Ashkelon">
       Ascalon
      </a>
      in Jund Filastin and the town Sariphaea in
      <a href="/wiki/Jund_al-Urdunn" title="Jund al-Urdunn">
       Jund al-Urdunn
      </a>
      were completely destroyed in the conflict by
      <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">
       Bedouin
      </a>
      tribes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gil283_149-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gil283-149">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        149
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Several towns and villages in western Palestine were also sacked.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
       <a href="#cite_note-150">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        150
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The monasteries of St. Chariton, St. Cyriacus, St. Sabas,
      <a href="/wiki/Al-Ubeidiya" title="Al-Ubeidiya">
       St. Theodosius
      </a>
      , and St. Euthymius were also attacked.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Patrich65_151-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Patrich65-151">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        151
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The combined casualties of the tribal federations totalled roughly 1,200.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SERK22_152-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SERK22-152">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        152
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During
      <a href="/wiki/Harun_al-Rashid" title="Harun al-Rashid">
       Harun al-Rashid
      </a>
      's (786809) reign the first formal contacts with the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankish_Kingdom" title="Frankish Kingdom">
       Frankish Kingdom
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">
       Charlemagne
      </a>
      occurred, as part of the attempted
      <a href="/wiki/Abbasid%E2%80%93Carolingian_alliance" title="AbbasidCarolingian alliance">
       AbbasidCarolingian alliance
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
       <a href="#cite_note-153">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        153
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 797,
      <a href="/wiki/Harun_al-Rashid" title="Harun al-Rashid">
       Harun al-Rashid
      </a>
      is reported to have offered the custody of the Christian holy places in
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      to Charlemagne, in return for Charlemagne sending money for construction and improvements.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
       <a href="#cite_note-154">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        154
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As a result, the
      <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre" title="Church of the Holy Sepulchre">
       Church of the Holy Sepulchre
      </a>
      was restored and the Latin hospital was enlarged and placed under the control of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedictines" title="Benedictines">
       Benedictines
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
       <a href="#cite_note-155">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        155
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Two years later
      <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">
       Charlemagne
      </a>
      sent another mission to Patriarch George of
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
       <a href="#cite_note-156">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        156
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Towards the end of the 9th century, the Baghdad-based Abbasids began to lose control of their western provinces. From 878 Palestine was ruled from Egypt by semi-autonomous rulers for almost a century, beginning with
      <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_ibn_Tulun" title="Ahmad ibn Tulun">
       Ahmad ibn Tulun
      </a>
      , ruler of
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      and founder of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tulunid" title="Tulunid">
       Tulunid
      </a>
      dynasty, who conquered Palestine and most of
      <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
       Syria
      </a>
      four years after declaring
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      's independence from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasid" title="Abbasid">
       Abbasid
      </a>
      court in
      <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">
       Baghdad
      </a>
      . The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasids" title="Abbasids">
       Abbasids
      </a>
      regained direct control of Palestine in 904, after their invasion forced the army of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tulunid" title="Tulunid">
       Tulunid
      </a>
      Emir
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harun_of_Tulunids" title="Harun of Tulunids">
       Harun
      </a>
      to retreat to
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      where the
      <a href="/wiki/Tulunids" title="Tulunids">
       Tulunids
      </a>
      were defeated the following year.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Direct control from Baghdad was maintained until 939 when
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_bin_Tughj_Al-Ikhshid" title="Muhammad bin Tughj Al-Ikhshid">
       Muhammad bin Tughj Al-Ikhshid
      </a>
      , governor of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasid" title="Abbasid">
       Abbasid
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Palestine" title="Palestine">
       Palestine
      </a>
      , was granted independent control over his domain and the title Al-Ikhshid (Prince) by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasid" title="Abbasid">
       Abbasid
      </a>
      Caliph
      <a href="/wiki/Ar-Radi" title="Ar-Radi">
       Ar-Radi
      </a>
      . Like the Tulunids, the relative proximity of the Ikhshidid capital to Palestine resulted in a greater focus on the region, such that both Ikhshidid rulers,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_bin_Tughj_Al-Ikhshid" title="Muhammad bin Tughj Al-Ikhshid">
       Muhammad bin Tughj Al-Ikhshid
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Abu_al-Misk_Kafur" title="Abu al-Misk Kafur">
       Abu al-Misk Kafur
      </a>
      , were buried in Jerusalem.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The death of
      <a href="/wiki/Abu_al-Misk_Kafur" title="Abu al-Misk Kafur">
       Abu al-Misk Kafur
      </a>
      in 968 resulted in a fatal division of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ikhshidid" title="Ikhshidid">
       Ikhshidid
      </a>
      government as they prepared for the expected invasion by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimids" title="Fatimids">
       Fatimids
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Fatimid_Caliphate_period">
       <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">
        Fatimid Caliphate
       </a>
       period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Fatimid Caliphate period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fatimid_Caliphate.PNG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="983" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Fatimid_Caliphate.PNG/220px-Fatimid_Caliphate.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Fatimid_Caliphate.PNG/330px-Fatimid_Caliphate.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Fatimid_Caliphate.PNG/440px-Fatimid_Caliphate.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fatimid_Caliphate.PNG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Fatimid Caliphate at its greatest extent
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      From their base in
      <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">
       Tunisia
      </a>
      , General
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gawhar_Al-Siqilli" title="Gawhar Al-Siqilli">
       Gawhar Al-Siqilli
      </a>
      of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ismaili" title="Ismaili">
       Ismaili
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shi%27ite" title="Shi'ite">
       Shi'ite
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimid" title="Fatimid">
       Fatimids
      </a>
      , who claimed to be descendants of Muhammad through his daughter
      <a href="/wiki/Fatimah" title="Fatimah">
       Fatimah
      </a>
      , conquered the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ikhshidid" title="Ikhshidid">
       Ikhshidid
      </a>
      domains of
      <a href="/wiki/Palestine" title="Palestine">
       Palestine
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      in 969, following a treaty guaranteeing the local
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">
       Sunnis
      </a>
      freedom of religion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arabnet_157-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Arabnet-157">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        157
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They moved their capital to the new city of
      <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">
       Cairo
      </a>
      , just north of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ikhshidid" title="Ikhshidid">
       Ikhshidid
      </a>
      capital of
      <a href="/wiki/Fustat" title="Fustat">
       Fustat
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Fatimids continued their expansion to the borders of the
      <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
       Byzantine Empire
      </a>
      , and a failed attack on
      <a href="/wiki/Antioch" title="Antioch">
       Antioch
      </a>
      in 971 was followed up by a Byzantine defeat outside of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amida_(Roman_city)" title="Amida (Roman city)">
       Amida
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
       <a href="#cite_note-158">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        158
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the Byzantines fought back and in 975 Emperor
      <a href="/wiki/John_I_Tzimiskes" title="John I Tzimiskes">
       John I Tzimiskes
      </a>
      's second campaign took Syria and much of northern Palestine, including
      <a href="/wiki/Tiberias" title="Tiberias">
       Tiberias
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Nazareth" title="Nazareth">
       Nazareth
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caesarea_Palaestina" title="Caesarea Palaestina">
       Caesarea Palaestina
      </a>
      , but was defeated en route to Jerusalem. The emperor became ill and died suddenly in 976 on his return from the campaign, and the Byzantines withdrew shortly thereafter to face the Bulgar threat in the north of their empire.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
       <a href="#cite_note-159">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        159
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Jerusalem, Nablus, and Askalan were expanded and renovated under Fatimid rule.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp11_144-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp11-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, in 1009, Fatimid Caliph
      <a href="/wiki/Al-Hakim_bi-Amr_Allah" title="Al-Hakim bi-Amr Allah">
       Al-Hakim
      </a>
      ordered the destruction of all churches and synagogues in the empire, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre" title="Church of the Holy Sepulchre">
       Church of the Holy Sepulchre
      </a>
      . However, this was reversed twenty years later by the Al-Hakim' successor as Caliph,
      <a href="/wiki/Ali_az-Zahir" title="Ali az-Zahir">
       Ali az-Zahir
      </a>
      , who authorized the rebuilding of the
      <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre" title="Church of the Holy Sepulchre">
       Church of the Holy Sepulchre
      </a>
      and other Christian churches in a treaty with Byzantine Emperor
      <a href="/wiki/Romanos_III_Argyros" title="Romanos III Argyros">
       Romanos III Argyros
      </a>
      . Romanos' successor
      <a href="/wiki/Constantine_IX_Monomachos" title="Constantine IX Monomachos">
       Constantine IX Monomachos
      </a>
      paid for the restoration, and a number of other Christian buildings, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Muristan" title="Muristan">
       Muristan
      </a>
      hospital, church and monastery were built during this period. Az-Zahir also undertook a major renovation of the
      <a href="/wiki/Dome_of_the_Rock" title="Dome of the Rock">
       Dome of the Rock
      </a>
      during his reign. After the 10th century, the division of Palestine into
      <i>
       Junds
      </i>
      began to break down.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shahinp11_144-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shahinp11-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During the early 11th century,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seljuk_Turks" title="Seljuk Turks">
       Seljuk Turks
      </a>
      invaded large portions of West Asia and both the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimid" title="Fatimid">
       Fatimids
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
       Byzantines
      </a>
      suffered setbacks from the fighting. Warfare between the Fatimids and Seljuks caused great disruption for the local population and for western pilgrims. In 1073 Palestine was captured by
      <a href="/wiki/Malik-Shah_I" title="Malik-Shah I">
       Malik-Shah I
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Isfahan" title="Isfahan">
       Isfahan
      </a>
      -based
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Seljuq_Empire" title="Great Seljuq Empire">
       Great Seljuq Empire
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
       <a href="#cite_note-160">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        160
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      under Emir
      <a href="/wiki/Atsiz_ibn_Uvaq" title="Atsiz ibn Uvaq">
       Atsiz ibn Uvaq
      </a>
      , who was advancing south into the weakening
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimid_Empire" title="Fatimid Empire">
       Fatimid Empire
      </a>
      following the decisive defeat over the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine" title="Byzantine">
       Byzantine
      </a>
      army at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manzikert" title="Battle of Manzikert">
       Battle of Manzikert
      </a>
      two years previously and a devastating six-year famine in Egypt between 1067 and 1072.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Singh2002_p.455_161-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Singh2002_p.455-161">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        161
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Seljuk rule was unpopular, and in 1077 Jerusalem revolted against their rule while Emir
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Atsiz_ibd_Uvaq&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Atsiz ibd Uvaq (page does not exist)">
       Atsiz ibd Uvaq
      </a>
      was fighting the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimid_Empire" title="Fatimid Empire">
       Fatimid Empire
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      . On his return to Jerusalem, Atsiz re-took the city and massacred the local population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bosworth2007_p._234_162-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bosworth2007_p._234-162">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        162
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As a result, Atsiz was executed by the governor of
      <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
       Syria
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Tutush_I" title="Tutush I">
       Tutush I
      </a>
      , the brother of
      <a href="/wiki/Seljuq_dynasty" title="Seljuq dynasty">
       Seljuk
      </a>
      leader
      <a href="/wiki/Malik-Shah_I" title="Malik-Shah I">
       Malik-Shah I
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Tutush_I" title="Tutush I">
       Tutush I
      </a>
      appointed
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artuqid_dynasty" title="Artuqid dynasty">
       Artuq bin Ekseb
      </a>
      , later founder of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artuqid_dynasty" title="Artuqid dynasty">
       Artuqid dynasty
      </a>
      , as governor.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artuqid_dynasty" title="Artuqid dynasty">
       Artuq bin Ekseb
      </a>
      died in 1091, and was succeeded as governor by his sons
      <a href="/wiki/Ilghazi" title="Ilghazi">
       Ilghazi
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ahlatshahs" title="Ahlatshahs">
       Sokmen
      </a>
      , known as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artuqid_dynasty" title="Artuqid dynasty">
       Artuqid dynasty
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Malik-Shah_I" title="Malik-Shah I">
       Malik Shah
      </a>
      died in 1092, and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Seljuk_Empire" title="Great Seljuk Empire">
       Great Seljuk Empire
      </a>
      split into smaller warring states. Control of Palestine was disputed between
      <a href="/wiki/Duqaq" title="Duqaq">
       Duqaq
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Fakhr_al-Mulk_Radwan" title="Fakhr al-Mulk Radwan">
       Radwan
      </a>
      after the death of their father
      <a href="/wiki/Tutush_I" title="Tutush I">
       Tutush I
      </a>
      in 1095. The ongoing rivalry weakens
      <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
       Syria
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimid" title="Fatimid">
       Fatimid
      </a>
      Regent
      <a href="/wiki/Al-Afdal_Shahanshah" title="Al-Afdal Shahanshah">
       Al-Afdal Shahanshah
      </a>
      recaptured the region in 1098 from the
      <a href="/wiki/Artuqids" title="Artuqids">
       Artuqids
      </a>
      , just before the arrival of the crusaders.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
       <a href="#cite_note-163">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        163
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1054, the
      <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="EastWest Schism">
       Great Schism
      </a>
      formally divided the Christian church into east and west, resulting in the holy sites of Palestine falling under the jurisdiction of the
      <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">
       Eastern Orthodox Church
      </a>
      . However, in 1090, Byzantine Emperor
      <a href="/wiki/Alexios_I_Komnenos" title="Alexios I Komnenos">
       Alexios I Komnenos
      </a>
      began taking reconciliatory measures towards the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papacy" title="Papacy">
       Papacy
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
       <a href="#cite_note-164">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        164
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with the intention of seeking western support against the Seljuqs. In 1095 his ambassadors appeared before
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_Urban_II" title="Pope Urban II">
       Pope UrbanII
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Piacenza" title="Council of Piacenza">
       Council of Piacenza
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canduci.2C_pg._279_165-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Canduci.2C_pg._279-165">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        165
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      to request
      <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">
       mercenary
      </a>
      forces, and later that year at the
      <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Clermont" title="Council of Clermont">
       Council of Clermont
      </a>
      Pope
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_II" title="Urban II">
       Urban II
      </a>
      called for the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Crusade" title="First Crusade">
       First Crusade
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Jerusalem_.28Crusaders.29_period">
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">
        Kingdom of Jerusalem (Crusaders)
       </a>
       period
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Jerusalem (Crusaders) period">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Near_East_1135.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1315" data-file-width="955" height="413" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Near_East_1135.svg/300px-Near_East_1135.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Near_East_1135.svg/450px-Near_East_1135.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Near_East_1135.svg/600px-Near_East_1135.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Near_East_1135.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The kingdom of Jerusalem and the other Crusader states at their height in 1135
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Byzantine_Empire,_c.1180.PNG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="370" data-file-width="801" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/The_Byzantine_Empire%2C_c.1180.PNG/220px-The_Byzantine_Empire%2C_c.1180.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/The_Byzantine_Empire%2C_c.1180.PNG/330px-The_Byzantine_Empire%2C_c.1180.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/The_Byzantine_Empire%2C_c.1180.PNG/440px-The_Byzantine_Empire%2C_c.1180.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Byzantine_Empire,_c.1180.PNG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Crusader states shortly before their fall in 1180
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Crusades" title="The Crusades">
       The Crusades
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">
       Kingdom of Jerusalem
      </a>
      was a
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christian
      </a>
      kingdom established in the
      <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">
       Levant
      </a>
      in 1099 as a result of the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Crusade" title="First Crusade">
       First Crusade
      </a>
      . Its control of Jerusalem and most of Palestine lasted almost a century until defeat by
      <a href="/wiki/Saladin" title="Saladin">
       Saladin
      </a>
      's forces in 1187, after which most of Palestine was controlled by the Ayyubids.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Shortly after Crusader rule was established in Palestine,
      <a href="/wiki/Godfrey_of_Bouillon" title="Godfrey of Bouillon">
       Godfrey of Bouillon
      </a>
      promised to turn over the rule of the region to the Papacy once the crusaders had captured
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      . However, the invasion of Egypt did not occur as Godfrey died shortly thereafter and
      <a href="/wiki/Baldwin_I_of_Jerusalem" title="Baldwin I of Jerusalem">
       Baldwin
      </a>
      was proclaimed the first
      <a href="/wiki/King_of_Jerusalem" title="King of Jerusalem">
       King of Jerusalem
      </a>
      after politically outmanoeuvering
      <a href="/wiki/Dagobert_of_Pisa" title="Dagobert of Pisa">
       Dagobert of Pisa
      </a>
      who had previously been appointed as the Latin Patriarch.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        166
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At first the Crusader kingdom was little more than a loose collection of towns and cities captured during the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_crusade" title="First crusade">
       first crusade
      </a>
      . At its height, the kingdom roughly encompassed the territory of modern-day Israel and the State of Palestine. It extended from modern Lebanon in the north to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinai_Desert" title="Sinai Desert">
       Sinai Desert
      </a>
      in the south, and into modern Jordan and Syria in the east. There were also attempts to expand the kingdom into
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimid" title="Fatimid">
       Fatimid
      </a>
      Egypt. Its kings held a certain amount of authority over the other
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crusader_state" title="Crusader state">
       crusader states
      </a>
      to the north: the
      <a href="/wiki/County_of_Tripoli" title="County of Tripoli">
       County of Tripoli
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Antioch" title="Principality of Antioch">
       Principality of Antioch
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/County_of_Edessa" title="County of Edessa">
       County of Edessa
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Many customs and institutions were imported from the territories of Western Europe from which the crusaders came, and there were close familial and political connections with the West throughout the kingdom's existence. It was, however, a relatively minor kingdom in comparison and often lacked financial and military support from Europe. Locally based military orders were founded in the kingdom to fill this vacuum. The foundation of the
      <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">
       Knights Hospitaller
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Gerard_Thom" title="Gerard Thom">
       Gerard Thom
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Muristan" title="Muristan">
       Muristan
      </a>
      Christian hospice in Jerusalem was confirmed by a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papal_Bull" title="Papal Bull">
       Papal Bull
      </a>
      from
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paschal_II" title="Pope Paschal II">
       Pope Paschal II
      </a>
      in 1113, and the founding by
