     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/1922_census_of_Palestine" title="1922 census of Palestine">
       1922 census of Palestine
      </a>
      recorded the population of Palestine as 757,000, of which 78% were Muslims, 11% were Jews, 10% were Christians and 1% were Druze.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census1922_218-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Census1922-218">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        218
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the early years of the Mandate, Jewish immigration to Palestine was quite substantial. In April 1920, violent Arab disturbances against the Jews in Jerusalem occurred, which came to be known as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1920_Palestine_riots" title="1920 Palestine riots">
       1920 Palestine riots
      </a>
      . The riots followed rising tensions in Arab-Jewish relations over the implications of Zionist immigration. The British military administration's erratic response failed to contain the rioting, which continued for four days. As a result of the events, trust among the British, Jews, and Arabs eroded. One consequence was that the Jewish community increased moves towards an autonomous infrastructure and security apparatus parallel to that of the British administration.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In April 1920, the Allied Supreme Council (the United States, Great Britain, France, Italy and Japan) met at
      <a href="/wiki/San_Remo_conference" title="San Remo conference">
       Sanremo
      </a>
      and formal decisions were taken on the allocation of mandate territories. The United Kingdom obtained a mandate for Palestine and France obtained a mandate for Syria. The boundaries of the mandates and the conditions under which they were to be held were not decided. The Zionist Organization's representative at Sanremo,
      <a href="/wiki/Chaim_Weizmann" title="Chaim Weizmann">
       Chaim Weizmann
      </a>
      , subsequently reported to his colleagues in London:
     </p>
     <blockquote>
      <p>
       There are still important details outstanding, such as the actual terms of the mandate and the question of the boundaries in Palestine. There is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delimitation" title="Delimitation">
        delimitation
       </a>
       of the boundary between French Syria and Palestine, which will constitute the northern frontier and the eastern line of demarcation, adjoining Arab Syria. The latter is not likely to be fixed until the Emir Feisal attends the Peace Conference, probably in Paris.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219">
        <a href="#cite_note-219">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         219
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Winston_Churchill_and_Abdullah_I_of_Jordan_1921_(restored).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3837" data-file-width="5096" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Winston_Churchill_and_Abdullah_I_of_Jordan_1921_%28restored%29.jpg/220px-Winston_Churchill_and_Abdullah_I_of_Jordan_1921_%28restored%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Winston_Churchill_and_Abdullah_I_of_Jordan_1921_%28restored%29.jpg/330px-Winston_Churchill_and_Abdullah_I_of_Jordan_1921_%28restored%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Winston_Churchill_and_Abdullah_I_of_Jordan_1921_%28restored%29.jpg/440px-Winston_Churchill_and_Abdullah_I_of_Jordan_1921_%28restored%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Winston_Churchill_and_Abdullah_I_of_Jordan_1921_(restored).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Churchill and Abdullah (with Herbert Samuel) during their negotiations in Jerusalem, March 1921
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In July 1920, the French drove
      <a href="/wiki/Faisal_I_of_Iraq" title="Faisal I of Iraq">
       Faisal bin Husayn
      </a>
      from Damascus, ending his already negligible control over the region of Transjordan, where local chiefs traditionally resisted any central authority. The sheikhs, who had earlier pledged their loyalty to the
      <a href="/wiki/Sharif_of_Mecca" title="Sharif of Mecca">
       Sharif of Mecca
      </a>
      , asked the British to undertake the region's administration.
      <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Samuel,_1st_Viscount_Samuel" title="Herbert Samuel, 1st Viscount Samuel">
       Herbert Samuel
      </a>
      asked for the extension of the Palestine government's authority to Transjordan, but at meetings in Cairo and Jerusalem between
      <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">
       Winston Churchill
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_I_of_Jordan" title="Abdullah I of Jordan">
       Emir Abdullah
      </a>
      in March 1921 it was agreed that Abdullah would administer the territory (initially for six months only) on behalf of the Palestine administration. In the summer of 1921 Transjordan was included within the Mandate, but excluded from the provisions for a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_National_Home" title="Jewish National Home">
       Jewish National Home
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220">
       <a href="#cite_note-220">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        220
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 24 July 1922, the League of Nations approved the terms of the British Mandate over Palestine and Transjordan. On 16 September the League formally
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transjordan_memorandum" title="Transjordan memorandum">
       approved a memorandum
      </a>
      from
      <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Balfour" title="Arthur Balfour">
       Lord Balfour
      </a>
      confirming the exemption of Transjordan from the clauses of the mandate concerning the creation of a Jewish national home and Jewish settlement.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221">
       <a href="#cite_note-221">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        221
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      With Transjordan coming under the administration of the British Mandate, the mandate's collective territory became constituted of 23% Palestine and 77% Transjordan. The mandate for Palestine, while specifying actions in support of Jewish immigration and political status, stated, in Article 25, that in the territory to the east of the Jordan River, Britain could 'postpone or withhold' those articles of the Mandate concerning a Jewish National Home. Transjordan was a very sparsely populated region (especially in comparison with Palestine proper) due to its relatively limited resources and largely desert environment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222">
       <a href="#cite_note-222">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        222
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223">
       <a href="#cite_note-223">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        223
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mandate_for_Palestine_(legal_instrument).svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1052" data-file-width="744" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Mandate_for_Palestine_%28legal_instrument%29.svg/220px-Mandate_for_Palestine_%28legal_instrument%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Mandate_for_Palestine_%28legal_instrument%29.svg/330px-Mandate_for_Palestine_%28legal_instrument%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Mandate_for_Palestine_%28legal_instrument%29.svg/440px-Mandate_for_Palestine_%28legal_instrument%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mandate_for_Palestine_(legal_instrument).svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Palestine and
        <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">
         Transjordan
        </a>
        were incorporated (under different legal and administrative arrangements) into the "Mandate for Palestine and Transjordan Memorandum" issued by the
        <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
         League of Nations
        </a>
        to
        <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">
         Great Britain
        </a>
        on 29 September 1923
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1923, an agreement between the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
       United Kingdom
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
       France
      </a>
      confirmed the border between the British Mandate of Palestine and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Mandate_of_Syria" title="French Mandate of Syria">
       French Mandate of Syria
      </a>
      . The British handed over the southern
      <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">
       Golan Heights
      </a>
      to the French in return for the northern Jordan Valley. The border was re-drawn so that both sides of the
      <a href="/wiki/Jordan_River" title="Jordan River">
       Jordan River
      </a>
      and the whole of the
      <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Galilee" title="Sea of Galilee">
       Sea of Galilee
      </a>
      , including a 10-metre-wide strip along the northeastern shore, were made a part of Palestine,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224">
       <a href="#cite_note-224">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        224
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with the provisions that Syria have fishing and navigation rights in the lake.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225">
       <a href="#cite_note-225">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        225
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Exploration_Fund" title="Palestine Exploration Fund">
       Palestine Exploration Fund
      </a>
      published surveys and maps of
      <a class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?q=survey%20of%20western%20palestine&amp;ie=UTF-8&amp;oe=utf-8&amp;rls=org.mozilla:en-US:official&amp;client=firefox-a&amp;um=1&amp;sa=N&amp;tab=wp" rel="nofollow">
       <b>
        Western Palestine
       </b>
      </a>
      (aka Cisjordan) starting in the mid-19th century. Even before the Mandate came into legal effect in 1923 (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1922_Text:_League_of_Nations_Palestine_Mandate" title="1922 Text: League of Nations Palestine Mandate">
       text
      </a>
      ), British terminology sometimes used '"Palestine" for the part west of the Jordan River and "Trans-Jordan" (or
      <i>
       Transjordania
      </i>
      ) for the part east of the Jordan River.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226">
       <a href="#cite_note-226">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        226
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227">
       <a href="#cite_note-227">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        227
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palestine_stamp.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="651" data-file-width="552" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Palestine_stamp.jpg/220px-Palestine_stamp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Palestine_stamp.jpg/330px-Palestine_stamp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Palestine_stamp.jpg/440px-Palestine_stamp.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palestine_stamp.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Rachel%27s_Tomb" title="Rachel's Tomb">
         Rachel's Tomb
        </a>
        on a 1927 British Mandate stamp. "Palestine" is shown in English, Arabic (
        <span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">
         
        </span>
        ), and Hebrew, the latter includes the acronym
        <span lang="he" xml:lang="he">
         
        </span>
        for
        <span lang="he-Latn" xml:lang="he-Latn">
         <i>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eretz_Yisrael" title="Eretz Yisrael">
           Eretz Yisrael
          </a>
         </i>
        </span>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The first reference to the Palestinians, without qualifying them as Arabs, is to be found in a document of the Permanent Executive Committee, composed of Muslims and Christians, presenting a series of formal complaints to the British authorities on 26 July 1928.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228">
       <a href="#cite_note-228">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        228
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure_and_development">
       Infrastructure and development
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Infrastructure and development">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Between 1922 and 1947, the annual growth rate of the Jewish sector of the economy was 13.2%, mainly due to immigration and foreign capital, while that of the Arab was 6.5%. Per capita, these figures were 4.8% and 3.6% respectively. By 1936, the Jewish sector had eclipsed the Arab one, and Jewish individuals earned 2.6 times as much as Arabs. In terms of human capital, there was a huge difference. For instance, the literacy rates in 1932 were 86% for the Jews against 22% for the Arabs, but Arab literacy was steadily increasing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229">
       <a href="#cite_note-229">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        229
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1933, Adolf Hitler came to power in Germany, Haavara agreement is in place between the Zionist Federation and the German government of the Third Reich to facilitate the emigration of German Jews.
     </p>
     <p>
      The office of "Mufti of Jerusalem", traditionally limited in authority and geographical scope, was refashioned by the British into that of "Grand Mufti of Palestine". Furthermore, a Supreme Muslim Council (SMC) was established and given various duties, such as the administration of religious endowments and the appointment of religious judges and local muftis. During the revolt (see below) the
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_Higher_Committee" title="Arab Higher Committee">
       Arab Higher Committee
      </a>
      was established as the central political organ of the Arab community of Palestine.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During the Mandate period, many factories were established and roads and railroads were built throughout the country. The Jordan River was harnessed for production of electric power and the Dead Sea was tapped for minerals
      <a href="/wiki/Potash" title="Potash">
       potash
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bromine" title="Bromine">
       bromine
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1936.E2.80.931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine">
       19361939 Arab revolt in Palestine
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 19361939 Arab revolt in Palestine">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine" title="19361939 Arab revolt in Palestine">
       19361939 Arab revolt in Palestine
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Sparked off by the death of
      <a href="/wiki/Sheikh" title="Sheikh">
       Shaykh
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Izz_ad-Din_al-Qassam" title="Izz ad-Din al-Qassam">
       Izz ad-Din al-Qassam
      </a>
      at the hands of the British police near
      <a href="/wiki/Jenin" title="Jenin">
       Jenin
      </a>
      in November 1935, in the years 19361939 the Arabs participated in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine" title="19361939 Arab revolt in Palestine">
       Great Uprising
      </a>
      to protest against British rule and against mass Jewish immigration. The revolt manifested in a
      <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_general_strike" title="Palestinian general strike">
       strike
      </a>
      and armed insurrection started sporadically, becoming more organized with time. Attacks were mainly directed at British strategic installations such as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans_Arabian_Pipeline" title="Trans Arabian Pipeline">
       Trans Arabian Pipeline
      </a>
      (TAP) and railways, and to a lesser extent against Jewish settlements, secluded Jewish neighbourhoods in the mixed cities, and Jews, both individually and in groups.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Violence abated for about a year while the
      <a href="/wiki/Peel_Commission" title="Peel Commission">
       Peel Commission
      </a>
      deliberated and eventually recommended partition of Palestine. With the Arab rejection of this proposal, the revolt resumed during the autumn of 1937. Violence continued throughout 1938 and eventually petered out in 1939.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The British responded to the violence by greatly expanding their military forces and clamping down on Arab dissent. "Administrative detention" (imprisonment without charges or trial), curfews, and house demolitions were among British practices during this period. More than 120 Arabs were sentenced to death and about 40 hanged. The main Arab leaders were arrested or expelled.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Haganah" title="Haganah">
        Haganah
       </a>
      </i>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">
       Hebrew
      </a>
      for "defense"), a Jewish paramilitary organization, actively supported British efforts to quell the insurgency, which reached 10,000 Arab fighters at their peak during the summer and fall of 1938. Although the British administration did not officially recognize the
      <i>
       Haganah
      </i>
      , the British security forces cooperated with it by forming the
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Settlement_Police" title="Jewish Settlement Police">
       Jewish Settlement Police
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Special_Night_Squads" title="Special Night Squads">
       Special Night Squads
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230">
       <a href="#cite_note-230">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        230
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrorist" title="Terrorist">
       terrorist
      </a>
      splinter group of the Haganah, called the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Irgun" title="Irgun">
        Irgun
       </a>
      </i>
      (or
      <i>
       Etzel
      </i>
      )
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231">
       <a href="#cite_note-231">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        231
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      adopted a policy of violent retaliation against Arabs for attacks on Jews.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232">
       <a href="#cite_note-232">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        232
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At a meeting in Alexandria in July 1937 between Jabotinsky and Irgun commander Col. Robert Bitker and chief-of-staff Moshe Rosenberg, the need for indiscriminate retaliation due to the difficulty of limiting operations to only the "guilty" was explained. The Irgun launched attacks against public gathering places such as markets and cafes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233">
       <a href="#cite_note-233">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        233
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="487" data-file-width="890" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg/220px-Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg/330px-Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg/440px-Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Arab revolt of 193639 in Palestine. A Jewish bus equipped with wire screens to protect civilian riders against rocks and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grenades" title="Grenades">
         grenades
        </a>
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
        thrown by militants.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The revolt did not achieve its goals, although it is "credited with signifying the birth of the Arab Palestinian identity".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HistoryOfPalestinianRevolts_234-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HistoryOfPalestinianRevolts-234">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        234
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is generally credited with forcing the issuance of the
      <a href="/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939" title="White Paper of 1939">
       White Paper of 1939
      </a>
      , which renounced Britain's intent of creating a Jewish National Home in Palestine, as proclaimed in the 1917
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration_of_1917" title="Balfour Declaration of 1917">
       Balfour Declaration
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Another outcome of the hostilities was the partial disengagement of the Jewish and Arab economies in Palestine, which were more or less intertwined until that time. For example, whereas the Jewish city of
      <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">
       Tel Aviv
      </a>
      previously relied on the nearby Arab seaport of
      <a href="/wiki/Jaffa" title="Jaffa">
       Jaffa
      </a>
      , hostilities dictated the construction of a separate Jewish-run seaport for Tel Aviv.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_and_Palestine">
       World War II and Palestine
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: World War II and Palestine">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      When the Second World War broke out, the Jewish population sided with Britain.
      <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">
       David Ben-Gurion
      </a>
      , head of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Agency" title="Jewish Agency">
       Jewish Agency
      </a>
      , defined the policy with what became a famous motto: "We will fight the war as if there were no White Paper, and we will fight the White Paper as if there were no war." While this represented the Jewish population as a whole, there were exceptions (see below).
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As in most of the Arab world, there was no unanimity among the Palestinian Arabs as to their position regarding the combatants in World War II. A number of leaders and public figures saw an
      <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">
       Axis
      </a>
      victory as the likely outcome and a way of securing Palestine back from the Zionists and the British.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohammad_Amin_al-Husayni" title="Mohammad Amin al-Husayni">
       Mohammad Amin al-Husayni
      </a>
      , Grand Mufti of Jerusalem, spent the rest of the war in
      <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
       Nazi Germany
      </a>
      and the occupied areas. About 6,000 Palestinian Arabs and 30,000 Palestinian Jews joined the British forces.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 10 June 1940, Italy declared war on the British Commonwealth and sided with Germany. Within a month, the Italians
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_bombings_on_Palestine_in_World_War_II" title="Italian bombings on Palestine in World War II">
       attacked Palestine from the air
      </a>
      , bombing
      <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">
       Tel Aviv
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">
       Haifa
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235">
       <a href="#cite_note-235">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        235
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1942, there was a period of anxiety for the
      <a href="/wiki/Yishuv" title="Yishuv">
       Yishuv
      </a>
      , when the forces of German General
      <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Rommel" title="Erwin Rommel">
       Erwin Rommel
      </a>
      advanced east in
      <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
       North Africa
      </a>
      towards the
      <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
       Suez Canal
      </a>
      and there was fear that they would conquer Palestine. This period was referred to as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/200_days_of_anxiety" title="200 days of anxiety">
       two hundred days of anxiety
      </a>
      . This event was the direct cause for the founding, with British support, of the
      <a href="/wiki/Palmach" title="Palmach">
       Palmach
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236">
       <a href="#cite_note-236">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        236
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      a highly trained regular unit belonging to
      <a href="/wiki/Haganah" title="Haganah">
       Haganah
      </a>
      (which was mostly made up of reserve troops).
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JB_HQ.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="177" data-file-width="257" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bb/JB_HQ.jpg/220px-JB_HQ.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/bb/JB_HQ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/bb/JB_HQ.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JB_HQ.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Jewish Brigade headquarters under both
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Flag" title="Union Flag">
         Union Flag
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Israel" title="Flag of Israel">
         Jewish flag
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 3 July 1944, the British government consented to the establishment of a
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Brigade" title="Jewish Brigade">
       Jewish Brigade
      </a>
      with hand-picked Jewish and also non-Jewish senior officers. The brigade fought in Europe, most notably against the
      <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
       Germans
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
       Italy
      </a>
      from March 1945 until the end of the war in May 1945. Members of the Brigade played a key role in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berihah" title="Berihah">
       Berihah
      </a>
      's efforts to help Jews escape Europe for Palestine. Later, veterans of the Jewish Brigade became key participants of the new
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Israel" title="State of Israel">
       State of Israel
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">
       Israel Defense Forces
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Starting in 1939 and throughout the war and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">
       Holocaust
      </a>
      , the British reduced the number of Jewish immigrants allowed into Palestine, following the publication of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MacDonald_White_Paper" title="MacDonald White Paper">
       MacDonald White Paper
      </a>
      . Once the 15,000 annual quota was exceeded, Jews fleeing Nazi persecution were placed in detention camps or deported to places such as
      <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">
       Mauritius
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237">
       <a href="#cite_note-237">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        237
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1944
      <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Begin" title="Menachem Begin">
       Menachem Begin
      </a>
      assumed the
      <a href="/wiki/Irgun" title="Irgun">
       Irgun
      </a>
      's leadership, determined to force the British government to remove its troops entirely from Palestine. Citing that the British had reneged on their original promise of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration,_1917" title="Balfour Declaration, 1917">
       Balfour Declaration
      </a>
      , and that the
      <a href="/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939" title="White Paper of 1939">
       White Paper of 1939
      </a>
      restricting Jewish immigration was an escalation of their pro-Arab policy, he decided to break with the Haganah. Soon after he assumed command, a formal 'Declaration of Revolt' was publicized, and armed attacks against British forces were initiated.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LEHI" title="LEHI">
       Lehi
      </a>
      , another splinter group, opposed cessation of operations against the British authorities all along. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Agency" title="Jewish Agency">
       Jewish Agency
      </a>
      , which opposed those actions and the challenge to its role as government in preparation responded with "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Hunting_Season" title="The Hunting Season">
       The Hunting Season
      </a>
      "severe actions against supporters of the Irgun and Lehi, including turning them over to the British.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The country developed economically during the war, with increased industrial and agricultural outputs and the period was considered an `economic Boom'. In terms of Arab-Jewish relations, these were relatively quiet times.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238">
       <a href="#cite_note-238">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        238
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_the_British_Mandate_1945.E2.80.931948">
       End of the British Mandate 19451948
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: End of the British Mandate 19451948">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British%E2%80%93Zionist_conflict" title="BritishZionist conflict">
       BritishZionist conflict
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palestine_Index_to_Villages_and_Settlements,_showing_Land_in_Jewish_Possession_as_at_31.12.44.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7022" data-file-width="4000" height="386" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Palestine_Index_to_Villages_and_Settlements%2C_showing_Land_in_Jewish_Possession_as_at_31.12.44.jpg/220px-Palestine_Index_to_Villages_and_Settlements%2C_showing_Land_in_Jewish_Possession_as_at_31.12.44.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Palestine_Index_to_Villages_and_Settlements%2C_showing_Land_in_Jewish_Possession_as_at_31.12.44.jpg/330px-Palestine_Index_to_Villages_and_Settlements%2C_showing_Land_in_Jewish_Possession_as_at_31.12.44.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Palestine_Index_to_Villages_and_Settlements%2C_showing_Land_in_Jewish_Possession_as_at_31.12.44.jpg/440px-Palestine_Index_to_Villages_and_Settlements%2C_showing_Land_in_Jewish_Possession_as_at_31.12.44.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palestine_Index_to_Villages_and_Settlements,_showing_Land_in_Jewish_Possession_as_at_31.12.44.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Map showing Jewish-owned land as of 31 December 1944, including land owned in full, shared in undivided land and State Lands under concession. This constituted 6% of the total land area, of which more than half was held by the
        <a href="/wiki/Jewish_National_Fund" title="Jewish National Fund">
         JNF
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Jewish_Colonization_Association" title="Palestine Jewish Colonization Association">
         PICA
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239">
         <a href="#cite_note-239">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          239
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bombe_Irgoun_29_dec_1947.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="326" data-file-width="400" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Bombe_Irgoun_29_dec_1947.jpg/220px-Bombe_Irgoun_29_dec_1947.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Bombe_Irgoun_29_dec_1947.jpg/330px-Bombe_Irgoun_29_dec_1947.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0d/Bombe_Irgoun_29_dec_1947.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bombe_Irgoun_29_dec_1947.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Arab autobus after an attack by
        <a href="/wiki/Irgun" title="Irgun">
         Irgun
        </a>
        , 29 December 1947
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the years following
      <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
       World War II
      </a>
      , Britain's control over Palestine became increasingly tenuous. This was caused by a combination of factors, including:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       World public opinion turned against Britain as a result of the British policy of preventing
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">
        Holocaust
       </a>
       survivors from reaching Palestine, sending them instead to
       <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_internment_camps" title="Cyprus internment camps">
        Cyprus internment camps
       </a>
       , or even back to
       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
        Germany
       </a>
       , as in the case of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exodus_(ship)" title="Exodus (ship)">
        Exodus 1947
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       The costs of maintaining an army of over 100,000 men in Palestine weighed heavily on a British economy suffering from post-war depression, and was another cause for British public opinion to demand an end to the Mandate.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240">
        <a href="#cite_note-240">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         240
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Rapid deterioration due to the actions of the Jewish paramilitary organizations (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hagana" title="Hagana">
        Hagana
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Irgun" title="Irgun">
        Irgun
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lehi_(group)" title="Lehi (group)">
        Lehi
       </a>
       ), involving attacks on strategic installations (by all three) as well as on British forces and officials (by the Irgun and Lehi). This caused severe damage to British morale and prestige, as well as increasing opposition to the mandate in Britain itself, public opinion demanding to "bring the boys home".
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       The U.S. Congress was delaying a loan necessary to prevent British bankruptcy. The delays were in response to the British refusal to fulfill a promise given to Truman that 100,000 Holocaust survivors would be allowed to emigrate to Palestine.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      In early 1947 the British Government announced their desire to terminate the Mandate, and asked the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">
       United Nations General Assembly
      </a>
      to make recommendations regarding the future of the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241">
       <a href="#cite_note-241">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        241
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The British Administration declined to accept the responsibility for implementing any solution that wasn't acceptable to both the Jewish and the Arab communities, or to allow other authorities to take over responsibility for public security prior to the termination of its mandate on 15 May 1948.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242">
       <a href="#cite_note-242">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        242
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="UN_partition_and_the_1948_Palestine_War">
       UN partition and the 1948 Palestine War
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: UN partition and the 1948 Palestine War">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="infobox" style="clear:right; float:right; margin:0px 0px 15px 15px;">
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">

           </b>
          </th>
         </tr>

            </a>
            <br/>
            <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_refugee" title="Palestinian refugee">
             Palestinian refugee
            </a>
            <br/>
            <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_right_of_return" title="Palestinian right of return">
             Palestinian right of return
            </a>
            <br/>
            <a href="/wiki/Present_absentee" title="Present absentee">
             Present absentee
            </a>
            <br/>
            <a href="/wiki/Transfer_Committee" title="Transfer Committee">
             Transfer Committee
            </a>
            <br/>
            <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_194" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 194">
             Resolution 194
            </a>
            <br/>
           </p>
          </td>
         </tr>

             </li>
             <li class="nv-talk">

              <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Nakba&amp;action=edit">
