     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">
       United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War" title="1948 ArabIsraeli War">
       1948 ArabIsraeli War
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UN_Partition_Plan_Palestine.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1147" data-file-width="627" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/UN_Partition_Plan_Palestine.png/170px-UN_Partition_Plan_Palestine.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/UN_Partition_Plan_Palestine.png/255px-UN_Partition_Plan_Palestine.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/UN_Partition_Plan_Palestine.png/340px-UN_Partition_Plan_Palestine.png 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UN_Partition_Plan_Palestine.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        UN partition plan, 1947
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 29 November 1947, the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
       United Nations
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly" title="UN General Assembly">
       General Assembly
      </a>
      , voting 33 to 13 in favour with 10 abstentions, adopted a
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">
       resolution
      </a>
      , Resolution 181 (II), recommended a partition with Economic Union of Mandatory
      <a href="/wiki/Palestine" title="Palestine">
       Palestine
      </a>
      to follow the termination of the
      <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">
       British Mandate
      </a>
      . The plan was to partition Palestine into
      <i>
       Independent Arab state alongside a Jewish States, and the Special International Regime for the City of Jerusalem
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243">
       <a href="#cite_note-243">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        243
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Jerusalem was to encompass
      <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem" title="Bethlehem">
       Bethlehem
      </a>
      . Zionist leaders (including the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Agency" title="Jewish Agency">
       Jewish Agency
      </a>
      ), accepted the plan, while Palestinian Arab leaders rejected it and all independent Muslim and Arab states voted against it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244">
       <a href="#cite_note-244">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        244
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245">
       <a href="#cite_note-245">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        245
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246">
       <a href="#cite_note-246">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        246
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Almost immediately, sectarian violence erupted and spread, killing hundreds of Arabs, Jews and British over the ensuing months.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The rapid evolution of events precipitated into a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1947%E2%80%931948_Civil_War_in_Mandatory_Palestine" title="19471948 Civil War in Mandatory Palestine">
       Civil War
      </a>
      . For four months, under continuous Arab provocation and attack, the Yishuv was usually on the defensive while occasionally retaliating.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247">
       <a href="#cite_note-247">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        247
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Arab volunteers of the
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_Liberation_Army" title="Arab Liberation Army">
       Arab Liberation Army
      </a>
      entered Palestine to fight with the Palestinians, but the AprilMay offensive of
      <a href="/wiki/Yishuv" title="Yishuv">
       Yishuv
      </a>
      forces defeated the Arab forces and Arab Palestinian society collapsed. Some
      <a href="/wiki/1948_Palestinian_exodus" title="1948 Palestinian exodus">
       700,000 Palestinians
      </a>
      caught up in the turmoil fled or were driven from their homes.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948_2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="381" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948_2.jpg/220px-Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948_2.jpg/330px-Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b8/Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_State_of_Israel_1948_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">
         David Ben-Gurion
        </a>
        proclaiming independence beneath a large portrait of
        <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Herzl" title="Theodor Herzl">
         Theodor Herzl
        </a>
        , founder of modern
        <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">
         Zionism
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 14 May 1948,
      <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">
       David Ben-Gurion
      </a>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_People%27s_Council" title="Jewish People's Council">
       Jewish People's Council
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Declaration_of_the_Establishment_of_the_State_of_Israel" title="Declaration of the Establishment of the State of Israel">
       declared
      </a>
      <i>
       the establishment of a Jewish state in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eretz_Israel" title="Eretz Israel">
        Eretz Israel
       </a>
       (The Land of Israel), to be known as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Israel" title="State of Israel">
        State of Israel
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248">
       <a href="#cite_note-248">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        248
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The neighbouring Arab states intervened to prevent the partition and support the Palestinian Arab population. While Transjordan took control of territory designated for the future Arab State, Syrian, Iraqi and Egyptian expeditionary forces attacked Israel without success. The most intensive battles were waged between the Jordanian and Israeli forces over the control of Jerusalem.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On June 11, a truce was accepted by all parties. Israel used the lull to undertake a large-scale reinforcement of its army. In a series of military operations, during the war it conquered the whole of the Galilee region, both the Lydda and Ramle areas, and the Negev. It also managed to secure, in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battles_of_Latrun" title="Battles of Latrun">
       Battles of Latrun
      </a>
      , a road linking Jerusalem to Israel. However, the neighboring Arab countries signed the
      <a href="/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements" title="1949 Armistice Agreements">
       1949 Armistice Agreements
      </a>
      that ended the war, and have recognized de facto the new borders of Israel. In this phase, 350,000 more Arab Palestinians fled or were expelled from the conquered areas.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Partition_of_former_Mandatory_territory">
       Partition of former Mandatory territory
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Partition of former Mandatory territory">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_State_of_Israel" title="History of the State of Israel">
       History of the State of Israel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jordanian_occupation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Jordanian occupation of the West Bank">
       Jordanian occupation of the West Bank
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/All-Palestine_Government" title="All-Palestine Government">
       All-Palestine Government
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Gaza_Strip_by_Egypt" title="Occupation of the Gaza Strip by Egypt">
       Occupation of the Gaza Strip by Egypt
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Following the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1948_Arab-Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab-Israeli War">
       1948 Arab-Israeli War
      </a>
      , the area allocated to the Palestinian Arabs and the international zone of Jerusalem were occupied by Israel and the neighboring Arab states in accordance with the terms of the
      <a href="/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements" title="1949 Armistice Agreements">
       1949 Armistice Agreements
      </a>
      . In addition to the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">
       UN-partitioned area
      </a>
      allotted to the Jewish state, Israel captured and incorporated a further 26% of the British Mandate territory.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Jordan
      <a href="/wiki/Jordanian_occupation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Jordanian occupation of the West Bank">
       retained possession of about 21% of the former Mandate territory
      </a>
      . Jerusalem was divided, with Jordan taking the eastern parts, including the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jerusalem%27s_Old_City_walls" title="Jerusalem's Old City walls">
       Old City
      </a>
      , and Israel taking the western parts. In addition, Syria held on to small slivers of the former Mandate territory to the south and east of the
      <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Galilee" title="Sea of Galilee">
       Sea of Galilee
      </a>
      , which had been allocated in the UN partition plan to the Jewish state.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      For a description of the massive population movements, Arab and Jewish, at the time of the 1948 war and over the following decades, see
      <a href="/wiki/1948_Palestinian_exodus" title="1948 Palestinian exodus">
       Palestinian exodus
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_exodus_from_Arab_lands" title="Jewish exodus from Arab lands">
       Jewish exodus from Arab lands
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Palestinian_governorship_in_Egyptian-controlled_Gaza">
       Palestinian governorship in Egyptian-controlled Gaza
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Palestinian governorship in Egyptian-controlled Gaza">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      On the same day that the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Israel" title="State of Israel">
       State of Israel
      </a>
      was announced, the Arab League announced that it would set up a single Arab civil administration throughout Palestine,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249">
       <a href="#cite_note-249">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        249
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250">
       <a href="#cite_note-250">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        250
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and launched an attack on the new Israeli state.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/All-Palestine_Government" title="All-Palestine Government">
       All-Palestine Government
      </a>
      was established by the
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">
       Arab League
      </a>
      on 22 September 1948, during the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1948_Arab-Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab-Israeli War">
       1948 Arab-Israeli War
      </a>
      . It was soon recognized by all Arab League members, except Jordan. Though jurisdiction of the Government was declared to cover the whole of the former
      <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">
       Mandatory Palestine
      </a>
      , its effective jurisdiction was limited to the
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">
       Gaza Strip
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gelber177_251-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-gelber177-251">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        251
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Prime Minister of the Gaza-seated administration was named
      <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Hilmi_Pasha" title="Ahmed Hilmi Pasha">
       Ahmed Hilmi Pasha
      </a>
      , and the President was named
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hajj_Amin_al-Husseini" title="Hajj Amin al-Husseini">
       Hajj Amin al-Husseini
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252">
       <a href="#cite_note-252">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        252
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      former chairman of the
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_Higher_Committee" title="Arab Higher Committee">
       Arab Higher Committee
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The All-Palestine Government is regarded by some as the first attempt to establish an independent Palestinian state. It was under official Egyptian protection,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gelber177_251-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-gelber177-251">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        251
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but on the other hand it had no executive role, but rather mostly political and symbolic.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gelber177_251-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-gelber177-251">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        251
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Its importance gradually declined, especially due to relocation of seat of government from Gaza to Cairo following the Israeli invasion in late 1948. Though Gaza Strip returned under Egyptian control later on through the war, the All-Palestine Government remained in-exile in Cairo, managing Gazan affairs from outside.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1959, the All-Palestine Government was officially merged into the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Republic" title="United Arab Republic">
       United Arab Republic
      </a>
      , coming under formal
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_occupation_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Egyptian occupation of the Gaza Strip">
       Egyptian military administration
      </a>
      , with the appointment of Egyptian military administrators in Gaza. Egypt, however, both formally and informally denounced any and all territorial claims to Palestinian territory, in contrast to the government of Transjordan, which declared its annexation of the Palestinian West Bank. The All-Palestine Government's credentials as a
      <i>
       bona fide
      </i>
      sovereign state were questioned by many, particularly due to the effective reliance upon not only Egyptian military support, but Egyptian political and economic power.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Annexation_of_the_West_Bank_of_Jordan">
       Annexation of the West Bank of Jordan
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Annexation of the West Bank of Jordan">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Shortly after the proclamation of
      <a href="/wiki/All-Palestine_Government" title="All-Palestine Government">
       All-Palestine Government
      </a>
      in Gaza, the
      <a href="/wiki/Jericho_Conference" title="Jericho Conference">
       Jericho Conference
      </a>
      named
      <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_I_of_Jordan" title="Abdullah I of Jordan">
       King Abdullah I
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">
       Transjordan
      </a>
      , "King of Arab Palestine".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253">
       <a href="#cite_note-253">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        253
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Congress called for the union of Arab Palestine and Transjordan and Abdullah announced his intention to
      <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">
       annex
      </a>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">
       West Bank
      </a>
      . The other Arab League member states opposed Abdullah's plan.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/New_Historians" title="New Historians">
       New Historians
      </a>
      , like
      <a href="/wiki/Avi_Shlaim" title="Avi Shlaim">
       Avi Shlaim
      </a>
      , hold that there was an unwritten secret agreement between King Abdullah of Transjordan and Israeli authorities to partition the territory between themselves, and that this translated into each side limiting their objectives and exercising mutual restraint during the 1948 war.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shlaimp187_254-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shlaimp187-254">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        254
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The presence of a large number of immigrants and refugees from the now dissolved Mandate of Palestine fueled the regional ambitions of King Abdullah I, who sought control over what had been the British Jerusalem and Samaria districts on the west bank of Jordan River. Towards this goal the king granted Jordanian citizenship to all Arab holders of the Palestinian Mandate identity documents in February 1949, and outlawed the terms "Palestinian" and "Transjordanian" from official usage, changing the country's name from the Emirate of Trans-Jordan to the Hashemite Kingdom of Jordan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255">
       <a href="#cite_note-255">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        255
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The area east of the river became known as "al-iffah al-Sharqiyyal", or "The East Bank". In April 1950, with the formal annexation of the positions held by the Jordanian Army since 1948, the area became known as "al-iffah al-Gharbiyyal" or "The Western Bank".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256">
       <a href="#cite_note-256">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        256
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      With the formal union of the East and West Banks in 1950, the number of Palestinians in the kingdom rose by another 720,000, of whom 440,000 were West Bank residents and 280,000 were refugees from other areas of the former Mandate then living on the West Bank. Palestinians became the majority in Jordan although most believed their return to what was now the state of Israel was imminent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257">
       <a href="#cite_note-257">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        257
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Israeli_controlled_areas">
       Israeli controlled areas
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Israeli controlled areas">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-over_coverage" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <div style="width:52px">
         <img alt="Globe icon" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="350" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/48px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/73px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/97px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" title="Globe icon" width="48"/>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         The examples and perspective in this article or section might have an extensive
         <b>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">
           bias
          </a>
         </b>
         or disproportional coverage towards the West Bank and Gaza Strip.
         <span class="hide-when-compact">
          Please
          <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit">
           improve this article
          </a>
          or discuss the issue on the
          <a href="/wiki/Talk:History_of_Palestine" title="Talk:History of Palestine">
           talk page
          </a>
          .
         </span>
         <small>
          <i>
           (October 2012)
          </i>
         </small>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Israel did not retain the administrative structure of the Mandate, redrawing the district borders to roughly parallel the areas of responsibility of its military formations, then infantry brigades.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Six_Day_War_and_Yom_Kippur_War">
       Six Day War and Yom Kippur War
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Six Day War and Yom Kippur War">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Is-wb-gs-gh_v3.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2289" data-file-width="1428" height="353" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Is-wb-gs-gh_v3.png/220px-Is-wb-gs-gh_v3.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Is-wb-gs-gh_v3.png/330px-Is-wb-gs-gh_v3.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Is-wb-gs-gh_v3.png/440px-Is-wb-gs-gh_v3.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Is-wb-gs-gh_v3.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The region today:
        <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
         Israel
        </a>
        , the
        <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">
         West Bank
        </a>
        , the
        <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">
         Gaza Strip
        </a>
        and the
        <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">
         Golan Heights
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the course of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Six_Day_War" title="Six Day War">
       Six Day War
      </a>
      in June 1967, Israel captured the rest of the area that had been part of the British Mandate of Palestine, taking the West Bank (including East Jerusalem) from Jordan and the Gaza Strip from Egypt. Following military threats by Egypt and Syria, including Egyptian president Nasser's demand of the UN to remove its peace-keeping troops from the Egyptian-Israeli border, in June 1967 Israeli forces went to action against Egypt, Syria and Jordan. As a result of that war, the
      <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">
       Israel Defense Forces
      </a>
      conquered the
      <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">
       West Bank
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">
       Gaza Strip
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">
       Golan Heights
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">
       Sinai Peninsula
      </a>
      bringing them under
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_law" title="Military law">
       military rule
      </a>
      . Israel also pushed Arab forces back from East Jerusalem, which Jews had not been permitted to visit during the prior Jordanian rule. East Jerusalem was allegedly
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258">
       <a href="#cite_note-258">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        258
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      annexed by Israel as part of its capital, though this action has not been recognized internationally.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Israel also started building
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_settlement" title="Israeli settlement">
       settlements
      </a>
      on the occupied land.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259">
       <a href="#cite_note-259">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        259
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The United Nation's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Security_Council" title="Security Council">
       Security Council
      </a>
      passed
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resolution_242" title="Resolution 242">
       Resolution 242
      </a>
      , promoting the "
      <a href="/wiki/Land_for_peace" title="Land for peace">
       land for peace
      </a>
      " formula, which called for Israeli withdrawal from territories occupied in 1967, in return for the end of all states of belligerency by the aforementioned
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">
       Arab League
      </a>
      nations. Palestinians continued longstanding demands for the destruction of Israel or made a new demand for self-determination in a separate independent Arab state in the West Bank and Gaza Strip similar to but smaller than the original Partition area that Palestinians and the Arab League had rejected for statehood in 1947.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the course of 1973
      <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">
       Yom Kippur War
      </a>
      , military forces of Egypt crossed the Suez canal and Syria to regain the Golan heights. The attacking military forces of Syria were pushed back. After a cease fire, Egyptian President Sadat
      <a href="/wiki/Anwar_Sadat" title="Anwar Sadat">
       Anwar Sadat
      </a>
      started peace talks with the U.S. and Israel. Israel returned the
      <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">
       Sinai Peninsula
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      as part of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1978_Camp_David_Peace_Accords_between_Egypt_and_Israel" title="1978 Camp David Peace Accords between Egypt and Israel">
       1978 Camp David Peace Accords between Egypt and Israel
      </a>
      in hopes of establishing a genuine peace.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="First_Intifada.2C_Oslo_Accords_and_Palestinian_Authority">
       First Intifada, Oslo Accords and Palestinian Authority
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: First Intifada, Oslo Accords and Palestinian Authority">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      From 1987 to 1993, the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Intifada" title="First Intifada">
       First Palestinian Intifada
      </a>
      against Israel took place. Attempts at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace_process_in_the_Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Peace process in the Israeli-Palestinian conflict">
       peace process in the Israeli-Palestinian conflict
      </a>
      were made at the
      <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Conference_of_1991" title="Madrid Conference of 1991">
       Madrid Conference of 1991
      </a>
      . As the process progressed, in 1993 the Israelis allowed Chairman and President of the
      <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">
       Palestine Liberation Organization
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yassir_Arafat" title="Yassir Arafat">
       Yassir Arafat
      </a>
      to return to the region.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Following the historic
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1993_Oslo_Peace_Accords_between_Palestinians_and_Israel" title="1993 Oslo Peace Accords between Palestinians and Israel">
       1993 Oslo Peace Accords between Palestinians and Israel
      </a>
      (the "Oslo Accords"), which gave the Palestinian Arabs limited self-rule in some parts of the occupied territories
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260">
       <a href="#cite_note-260">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        260
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      through the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority">
       Palestinian Authority
      </a>
      , and other detailed negotiations,
      <a href="/wiki/Proposals_for_a_Palestinian_state" title="Proposals for a Palestinian state">
       proposals for a Palestinian state
      </a>
      gained momentum. They were soon followed in 1993 by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel-Jordan_Treaty_of_Peace" title="Israel-Jordan Treaty of Peace">
       Israel-Jordan Treaty of Peace
      </a>
      . To date, efforts to resolve the conflict have ended in deadlock, and the people of the region, Jews and Arabs, are engaged in a bloody conflict, called variously the "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab-Israeli_conflict" title="Arab-Israeli conflict">
       Arab-Israeli conflict
      </a>
      " or "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">
       Israeli-Palestinian conflict
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Intifada_and_later">
       Second Intifada and later
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Second Intifada and later">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      After few years of on-and-off negotiations, the Palestinians began an uprising against Israel. This was known as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Intifada" title="Al-Aqsa Intifada">
       Al-Aqsa Intifada
      </a>
      . The events were highlighted in world media by Palestinian suicide bombings in Israel that killed many civilians, and by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Security_Forces" title="Israeli Security Forces">
       Israeli Security Forces
      </a>
      full-fledged invasions into civilian areas
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baroud2007_261-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-baroud2007-261">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        261
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      along with some
      <a href="/wiki/Targeted_killing" title="Targeted killing">
       targeted killings
      </a>
      of Palestinian militant leaders and organizers. Israel began building a complex
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier" title="Israeli West Bank barrier">
       security barrier
      </a>
      to block suicide bombers invading into Israel from the West Bank in 2002.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Also in 2002, the
      <a href="/wiki/Road_map_for_peace" title="Road map for peace">
       Road map for peace
      </a>
      calling for the resolution of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">
       Israeli-Palestinian conflict
      </a>
      was proposed by a "quartet": the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
       European Union
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
       Russia
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
       United Nations
      </a>
      .
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States_of_America" title="President of the United States of America">
       U.S. President
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">
       George W. Bush
      </a>
      in a speech on June 24, 2002 called for an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_Palestinian_state" title="Independent Palestinian state">
       independent Palestinian state
      </a>
      living side by side with
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israel
      </a>
      in peace. Bush was the first U.S. President to explicitly call for such a Palestinian state.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Following
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel%27s_unilateral_disengagement_plan_of_2004" title="Israel's unilateral disengagement plan of 2004">
       Israel's unilateral disengagement plan of 2004
      </a>
      , it withdrew all settlers and most of the military presence from the Gaza strip, but maintained control of the air space and coast. Israel also dismantled four settlements in northern West Bank in September 2005. Following Israel's withdrawal, Palestinian militia groups fired
      <a href="/wiki/Qassam_rocket" title="Qassam rocket">
       Qassam rockets
      </a>
      into Israel and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smuggling_tunnels" title="Smuggling tunnels">
       smuggled
      </a>
      weapons and ammunition into Gaza from
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      . After the kidnap of Israeli soldiers in June 2006, Israel launched a military operation and reentered some parts of the Gaza Strip. Amidst severe criticism, they built the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier" title="Israeli West Bank barrier">
       Israeli West Bank barrier
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Following the January 2006 election of the
      <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">
       Hamas
      </a>
      government, Fatah resistance took the form of street battles that resulted in a victory for Hamas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baroud2007_261-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-baroud2007-261">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        261
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262">
       <a href="#cite_note-262">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        262
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Hamas took over the ministries of the (Fatah) Palestinian Authority and Gaza became a Hamas enclave outside PA control.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of July 2009, approximately 305,000 Israelis lived in 121 settlements in the West Bank.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haaretz-27July2009_263-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-haaretz-27July2009-263">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        263
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The 2.4 million
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      West Bank Palestinians (according to Palestinian evaluations) live primarily in four blocs centered in
      <a href="/wiki/Hebron" title="Hebron">
       Hebron
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">
       Ramallah
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Nablus" title="Nablus">
       Nablus
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Jericho" title="Jericho">
       Jericho
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Non-member_status_of_State_of_Palestine">
       Non-member status of State of Palestine
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Non-member status of State of Palestine">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="International recognition of the State of Palestine">
       International recognition of the State of Palestine
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">
       State of Palestine
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PLO" title="PLO">
       PLO
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 23 September 2011, President
      <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">
       Mahmoud Abbas
      </a>
      on behalf of the Palestine Liberation Organisation submitted an application for membership of Palestine in the United Nations. The campaign, dubbed "Palestine 194",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264">
       <a href="#cite_note-264">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        264
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      was formally backed by the Arab League in May,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alplan_265-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-alplan-265">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        265
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and was officially confirmed by the PLO on 26 June.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266">
       <a href="#cite_note-266">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        266
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The decision was labelled by the Israeli government as a unilateral step, while the Palestinian government countered that it is essential to overcoming the current impasse. Several other countries, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
       Germany
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
       Canada
      </a>
      , have also denounced the decision and called for a prompt return to negotiations. Many others, however, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">
       Norway
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
       Russia
      </a>
      , have endorsed the plan, as has
      <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">
       Secretary-General
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">
       Ban Ki-moon
      </a>
      , who stated, "UN members are entitled whether to vote for or against the Palestinian statehood recognition at the UN."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267">
       <a href="#cite_note-267">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        267
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In July 2012, it was reported that
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamas_Government_in_Gaza" title="Hamas Government in Gaza">
       Hamas Government in Gaza
      </a>
      was considering declaring the independence of the Gaza Strip with the help of Egypt.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-english.alarabiya.net_268-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-english.alarabiya.net-268">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        268
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In August 2012, Foreign Minister of the PNA Riyad al-Malki told reporters in Ramallah that PNA would renew effort to upgrade the Palestinian (PLO) status to "full member state" at the U.N. General Assembly on September 27, 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_269-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-269">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        269
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      By September 2012, with their application for full membership stalled due to the inability of Security Council members to "make a unanimous recommendation", Palestine had decided to pursue an upgrade in status from "observer entity" to
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers#Non-member_states" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">
       "non-member observer state"
      </a>
      . On November 27, it was announced that the appeal had been officially made, and would be put to a vote in the General Assembly on November 29, where their status upgrade was expected to be supported by a majority of states. In addition to granting Palestine "non-member observer state status", the draft resolution "expresses the hope that the Security Council will consider favourably the application submitted on 23 September 2011 by the State of Palestine for admission to full membership in the United Nations, endorses the two state solution based on the pre-1967 borders, and stresses the need for an immediate resumption of negotiations between the two parties".
     </p>
     <p>
      On November 29, 2012, in a 1389 vote (with 41 abstaining), General Assembly resolution 67/19 passed, upgrading Palestine to "non-member observer state" status in the United Nations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unispal1_270-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-unispal1-270">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        270
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera.com_271-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-aljazeera.com-271">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        271
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The new status equates Palestine's with that of the
      <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">
       Holy See
      </a>
      .The change in status was described by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">
        The Independent
       </a>
      </i>
      as "de facto recognition of the sovereign state of Palestine".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNStatehoodBid2012accepted_272-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UNStatehoodBid2012accepted-272">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        272
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The UN has permitted Palestine to title its representative office to the UN as "The Permanent Observer Mission of the State of Palestine to the United Nations",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273">
       <a href="#cite_note-273">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        273
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Palestine has started to re-title its name accordingly on postal stamps, official documents and passports,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera.com_271-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-aljazeera.com-271">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        271
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274">
       <a href="#cite_note-274">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        274
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      whilst it has instructed its diplomats to officially represent "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_State_of_Palestine" title="The State of Palestine">
       The State of Palestine
      </a>
      ", as opposed to the '
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestine_National_Authority" title="Palestine National Authority">
       Palestine National Authority
      </a>
      '.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera.com_271-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-aljazeera.com-271">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        271
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Additionally, on 17 December 2012, UN Chief of Protocol Yeocheol Yoon decided that "the designation of 'State of Palestine' shall be used by the Secretariat in all official United Nations documents",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275">
       <a href="#cite_note-275">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        275
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      thus recognising the PLO-proclaimed State of Palestine as being sovereign over the territories Palestine and its citizens under international law.
     </p>
     <p>
      As of February 2013, 131 (67.9%) of the 193 member states of the United Nations have recognised the State of Palestine. Many of the countries that do not recognise the State of Palestine nevertheless recognise the PLO as the 'representative of the Palestinian people'.
     </p>
     <h2>

        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Josephus: PACE:
         <a class="external text" href="http://pace-ancient.mcmaster.ca/york/york/showText?book=14&amp;chapter=5&amp;textChunk=whistonSection&amp;chunkId=4&amp;up.x=&amp;up.y=&amp;text=anti&amp;version=&amp;direction=&amp;tab=&amp;layout=english" rel="nofollow">

         </span>

         </a>
         , the third at Amathus, the fourth at

        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         "Josephus uses  for the first time in connection with the decree of the Roman governor of Syria, Gabinius (57 BCE), who abolished the constitution and the then existing form of government of Palestine and divided the country into five provinces, at the head of each of which a sanhedrin was placed ("Ant." xiv 5,  4)." via
         <a class="external text" href="http://jewishencyclopedia.com/view.jsp?artid=229&amp;letter=S&amp;search=Gabinius" rel="nofollow">
          Jewish Encyclopedia: Sanhedrin
         </a>
         :
        </span>
       </li>

         </i>
         , pp. 247-248: "Consequently, the province of Judea may be regarded as a satellite of Syria, though, in view of the measure of independence left to its governor in domestic affairs, it would be wrong to say that in the Julio-Claudian era Judea was legally part of the province of Syria."

         <b>

           ^

         <i>
          A History of the Jewish People
         </i>
         , H. H. Ben-Sasson editor, 1976, p. 247: "When Judea was converted into a Roman province [in 6 CE, p. 246], Jerusalem ceased to be the administrative capital of the country. The Romans moved the governmental residence and military headquarters to Caesarea. The centre of government was thus removed from Jerusalem, and the administration became increasingly based on inhabitants of the hellenistic cities (Sebaste, Caesarea and others)."

         <i>
          The archaeology of Ancient Judea and Palestine
         </i>
         . Getty Publications, 2005 p. 33. "It seems clear that by choosing a seemingly neutral name - one juxtaposing that of a neighboring province with the revived name of an ancient geographical entity (Palestine), already known from the writings of Herodotus - Hadrian was intending to suppress any connection between the Jewish people and that land."
         <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0892368004">
          ISBN 0-89236-800-4
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>

       <li id="cite_note-114">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-114">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.ccel.org/ccel/schaff/npnf214.vii.vi.x.html" rel="nofollow">
          Schaff's
          <i>
           Seven Ecumenical Councils
          </i>
          : First Nicaea: Canon VII
         </a>
         : "Since custom and ancient tradition have prevailed that the Bishop of
         <a href="/wiki/Aelia_Capitolina" title="Aelia Capitolina">
          Aelia
         </a>
         [i.e., Jerusalem] should be honored, let him, saving its due dignity to the Metropolis, have the next place of honor."; "It is very hard to determine just what was the "precedence" granted to the Bishop of Aelia, nor is it clear which is the "metropolis" referred to in the last clause. Most writers, including Hefele, Balsamon, Aristenus and Beveridge consider it to be
         <a href="/wiki/Caesarea_Maritima" title="Caesarea Maritima">
          Csarea
         </a>
         ; while Zonaras thinks Jerusalem to be intended, a view recently adopted and defended by Fuchs; others again suppose it is
         <a href="/wiki/Antioch" title="Antioch">
          Antioch
         </a>
         that is referred to."
        </span>
